Observations of this Court in AIIMS Students Union case (supra) highlight the importance of higher education and the modalities to be adopted for ensuring excellence are in the following words The Preamble to the Constitution of India secures, as one of its objects, fraternity assuring the dignity of the individual and the unity and integrity of the nation to we he people of India.	None
Reservation unless protected by the constitution itself, as given to us by the founding fathers and as adopted by the people of India, is subversion of fraternity, unity and integrity and dignity of the individual.	None
While dealing with Directive Principles of State Policy, Article 46 is taken note of often by overlooking Articles 41 and 47.	None
Article 41 obliges the State inter alia to make effective provision for securing the right to work and right to education.	None
Any reservation in favour of one, to the extent of reservation, is an inroad on the right of others to work and to learn.	None
Article 47 recognises the improvement of public health as one of the primary duties of the State.	None
Public health can be improved by having the best of doctors, specialists and super specialists.	None
Undergraduate level is a primary or basic level of education in medical sciences wherein reservation can be understood as the fulfilment of societal obligation of the State towards the weaker segments of the society.	None
Beyond this, a reservation is a reversion or diversion from the performance of primary duty of the State.	None
Permissible reservation at the lowest or primary rung is a step in the direction of assimilating the lesser fortunates in mainstream of society by bringing them to the level of others which they cannot achieve unless protectively pushed.	None
Once that is done the protection needs to be withdrawn in the own interest of protectees so that they develop strength and feel confident of stepping on higher rungs on their own legs shedding the crutches.	None
Pushing the protection of reservation beyond the primary level betrays bigwigs desire to keep the crippled crippled for ever.	None
Rabindra Nath Tagores vision of a free India cannot be complete unless knowledge is free and tireless striving stretches its arms towards perfection.	None
Almost a quarter century after the people of India have given the Constitution unto themselves, a chapter on fundamental duties came to be incorporated in the Constitution.	None
Fundamental duties, as defined in Article 51A, are not made enforceable by a writ of court just as the fundamental rights are, but it cannot be lost sight of that duties in Part IVA  Article 51A are prefixed by the same word fundamental which was prefixed by the founding fathers of the Constitution to rights in Part III.	None
Every citizen of India is fundamentally obliged to develop the scientific temper and humanism.	None
He is fundamentally duty bound to strive towards excellence in all spheres of individual and collective activity so that the nation constantly rises to higher levels of endeavour and achievements.	None
State is, all the citizens placed together and hence though Article 51A does not expressly cast any fundamental duty on the State, the fact remains that the duty of every citizen of India is the collective duty of the Sate.	None
Any reservation, apart from being sustainable on the constitutional anvil, must also be reasonable to be permissible.	None
In assessing the reasonability one of the factors to be taken into consideration would be  whether the character and quantum of reservation would stall or accelerate achieving the ultimate goal of excellence enabling the nation constantly rising to higher levels.	None
In the era of globalisation, where the nation as a whole has to compete with other nations of the world so as to survive, excellence cannot be given an unreasonable go by and certainly not compromised in its entirety.	None
Fundamental duties, though not enforceable by a writ of the court, yet provide a valuable guide and aid to interpretation of constitutional and legal issues.	None
In case of doubt or choice, peoples wish as manifested through Article 51A, can serve as a guide not only for resolving the issue but also for constructing or moulding the relief to be given by the courts.	None
Constitutional enactment of fundamental duties, if it has to have any meaning, must be used by courts as a tool to tab, even a taboo, on State action drifting away from constitutional values.	None
Respondents have vehemently contended that the concept of creamy layer may have relevance for the purpose of Article 16(4), but is really inconsequential so far as Articles 15(4) and 15(5) are concerned.	None
It is submitted that Article 16(4) is relatable to inadequate representation in Government services and in that context the well to do in the socially and educationally backward classes have to be excluded in view of the decisions of this Court.	None
But that logic cannot apply to the present dispute which relates to admissions to educational institutions.	None
Before considering the question as to the desirability of excluding creamy layer the concept of creamy layer needs to be focused upon.	None
Observations of this Court in various cases on this concept need to be noted.	None
In N.M.	None
Thomass case (supra) at page 363	None
, it was inter alia observed as follows A word of sociological caution.	None
In the light of experience, here and elsewhere, the danger of reservation, it seems to me, is threefold.	None
Its benefits, by and large, are snatched away by the top creamy layer of the backward caste or class, thus keeping the weakest among the weak always weak and leaving the fortunate layers to consume the whole cake.	None
Secondly, this claim is overplayed extravagantly in democracy by large and vocal groups whose burden of backwardness has been substantially lightened by the march of time and measures of better education and more opportunities of employment, but wish to wear the weaker section label as a means to score over their nearequals formally categorised as the upper brackets.	None
Lastly, a lasting solution to the problem comes only from improvement of social environment, added educational facilities and crossfertilisation of castes by intercaste and interclass marriages sponsored as a massive State programme, and this solution is calculatedly hidden from view by the higher backward groups with a vested interest in the plums of backwardism.	None
But social science research, not judicial impressionism, will alone tell the whole truth and a constant process of objective reevaluation of progress registered by the underdog categories is essential lest a once deserving reservation should be degraded into reverse discrimination.	None
Innovations in administrative strategy to help the really untouched, most backward classes also emerge from such sociolegal studies and audit exercises, if dispassionately made.	None
In fact, research conducted by the A.N. Sinha Institute of Social Studies, Patna, has revealed a dual society among harijans, a tiny elite gobbling up the benefits and the darker layers sleeping distances away from the special concessions.	None
For them, Articles 46 and 335 remain a noble romance, the bonanza going to the higher harijans.	None
I mention this in the present case because lower division clerks are likely to be drawn from the lowest levels of harijan humanity and promotion prospects being accelerated by withdrawing, for a time, test qualifications for this category may perhaps delve deeper.	None
An equalitarian breakthrough in a hierarchical structure has to use many weapons and Rule 13/AA perhaps is one.	None
Xx xx xx	None
It is platitudinous constitutional law that Articles 14 to 16 are a common code of guaranteed equality, the first laying down the broad doctrine, the other two applying it to sensitive areas historically important and politically polemical in a climate of communalism and jobbery.	None
In Vasant Kumars case (supra) at page 732 the view was reiterated in the following words In order to appreciate the view point advanced by Mr Desai which appeals to me both for its indepth study of the problem, and a fresh outlook on this vexed problem, at the outset let me take a look at the futuristic view of the Indian Society as envisaged in the Constitution.	None
No one is left in any doubt that the future Indian Society was to be casteless and classless.	None
Pandit Jawaharlal	None
Nehru the first Prime Minister of India said that Mahatma Gandhi has shaken the foundations of caste and the masses have been powerfully affected.	None
But an even greater power than Gandhi is at work, the conditions of modern life and it seems at last this hoary and tenacious ralic of past times must die.	None
Mahatma Gandhi, the Father of the Nation said, The caste system as we know is an anachronism.	None
It must go if both Hinduism and India are to live and grow from day to day.	None
In its onward march towards realising the constitutional goal, every attempt has to be made to destroy caste stratification.	None
Article 38(2) enjoins the State to strive to minimise the inequality in income and endeavour to eliminate inequalities in status, facilities and opportunities, not only amongst individuals but also amongst groups of people residing in different areas or engaged in different vocations.	None
Article 46 enjoins duty to promote with special care the educational and economic interests of the weaker sections of the people, and in particular of the Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes, and shall protect them from social injustice and all forms of exploitation.	None
Continued retention of the division of the society into various castes simultaneously introduces inequality of status.	None
And this inequality in status is largely responsible for retaining inequality in facilities and opportunities, ultimately resulting in bringing into existence an economically depressed class for transcending caste structure and caste barrier.	None
The society therefore was to be classless casteless society.	None
In order to set up such a society, steps have to be taken to weaken and progressively eliminate caste structure.	None
Unfortunately, the movement is in the reverse gear.	None
Caste stratification has become more rigid to some extent, and where concessions and preferred treatment schemes are introduced for economically disadvantaged classes, identifiable by caste label, the caste structure unfortunately received a fresh lease of life.	None
In fact there is a mad rush for being recognized as belonging to a caste which by its nomenclature would be included in the list of socially and educationally backward classes.	None
To illustrate Bakshi Commission in Gujarat recognized as many as 82 castes as being socially and educationally backward.	None
On the publication of its report, Government of Gujarat received representations by members of those castes who had not made any representation to the Bakshi Commission for treating them as socially and educationally backward.	None
This phenomenon was noticed by Mandal Commission when it observed Whereas the Commission has tried to make the Statewise lists of OBCs as comprehensive as possible, it is quite likely that several synonymy of the castes listed as backward have been left out.	None
Certain castes are known by a number of synonymy which vary from one region to the other and their complete coverage is almost impossible.	None
Mandal Commission found a way out by recommending that if a particular caste has been listed as backward then all its synonyms whether mentioned in the State lists or not should also be treated as backward.	None
Gujarat Government was forced to appoint a second commission known as Rane Commission.	None
Rane Commission took note of the fact that there was an organised effort for being considered socially and educationally backward castes.	None
Rane Commission recalled the observations in Balaji case that Social backwardness is on the ultimate analysis the result of poverty to a very large extent.	None
The Commission noticed that some of the castes just for the sake of being considered as socially and educationally backward, have degraded themselves to such an extent that, they had no hesitation in attributing different types of vices to and associating other factors indicative of backwardness, with their castes.	None
The Commission noted that the malaise requires to be remedied.	None
The Commission therefore, devised a method for determining socially and educationally backward classes without reference to caste, beneficial to all sections of people irrespective of the caste to which they belong.	None
The Commission came to an irrefutable conclusion that amongst certain castes and communities or class of people, only lower income groups amongst them are socially and educationally backward.	None
We may recall here a trite observation in case of N.M. Thomas which reads as under (SCC pg.363 para 124)	None
A word of sociological caution.	None
In the light of experience, here and elsewhere, the danger of reservation, it seems to me, is threefold.	None
Its benefits, by and large, are snatched away by the top creamy layer of the backward caste or class, thus keeping the weakest among the weak always weak and leaving the fortunate layers to consume the whole cake.	None
Secondly, this claim is overplayed extravagantly in democracy by large and vocal groups whose burden of backwardness has been substantially lightened by the march of time and measures of better education and more opportunities of employment, but wish to wear the weaker section label as a means to score over their nearequals formally categorised as the upper brackets.	None
A few other aspects for rejecting caste as the basis for identifying social and educational backwardness may be briefly noted.	None
If State patronage for preferred treatment accepts caste as the only insignia for determining social and educational backwardness, the danger looms large that this approach alone would legitimise and perpetuate caste system.	None
It does not go well with our proclaimed secular character as enshrined in the Preamble to the Constitution.	None
The assumption that all members of same caste a re equally socially and educationally backward is not wellfounded.	None
Such an approach provides an oversimplification of a complex problem of identifying the social and educational backwardness.	None
The Chairman of the Backward Classes Commission, set up in 1953, after having finalised the report, concluded that it would have been better if we could determine the criteria of backwardness on principles other than caste.	None
Lastly it is recognised without dissent that the caste based reservation has been usurped by the economically wellplaced section in the same caste.	None
To illustrate, it may be pointed that some years ago, I came across a petition for special leave against the decision of the Punjab and Haryana High Court in which the reservation of 2 per cent for admission to medical and engineering colleges in favour of Majhabi Sikhs was challenged by none other than the upper crust of the members of the Scheduled castes amongst Sikhs in Punjab, proving that the labeled weak exploits the really weaker.	None
Add to this, the findings of the Research Planning Scheme of sociologists assisting the Mandal Commission when it observed while determining the criteria of socially and educationally backward classes, social backwardness should be considered to be the critical element and educational backwardness to be the linked element though not necessarily derived from the former.	None
The team ultimately concluded that social backwardness refers to ascribed status, and it considered social backwardness as the critical element and educational backwardness to be the linked though not derived element.	None
The attempt is to identify socially and educationally backward classes of citizens.	Reasoning
The caste, as is understood in Hindu Society, is unknown to Muslims, Christians, Parsis, Jews etc.	None
Caste criterion would not furnish a reliable yardstick to identify socially and educationally backward group in the aforementioned communities though economic backwardness would.	None
Reservation in one or other form has been there for decades.	None
If a survey is made with reference to families in various castes considered to be socially and educationally backward, about the benefits of preferred treatment, it would unmistakably show that the benefits of reservations are snatched away by the top creamy layer of the backward castes.	None
This has to be avoided at any cost.	None
Significantly in Indra Sawhney No.1 it was emphatically noted as follows Society does not remain static.	None
The industrialisation and the urbanisation which necessarily followed in its wake, the advance on political, social and economic fronts made particularly after the commencement of the Constitution, the social reform movements of the last several decades, the spread of education and the advantages of the special provisions including reservations secured so far, have all undoubtedly seen at least some individuals and families in the backward classes, however small in number, gaining sufficient means to develop their capacities to compete with others in every field.	None
That is an undeniable fact.	None
Legally, therefore, they are not entitled to be any longer called as part of the backward classes whatever their original birthmark.	None
It can further hardly be argued that once a backward class, always a backward class.	None
That would defeat the very purpose of the special provisions made in the Constitution for the advancement of the backward classes, and for enabling them to come to the level of and to compete with the forward classes, as equal citizens.	None
On the other hand, to continue to confer upon such advanced sections from the backward classes the special benefits, would amount to treating equals unequally violating the equality provisions of the Constitution.	None
Secondly, to rank them with the rest of the backward classes would equally violate the right to equality of the rest in those classes, since it would amount to treating the unequals equally.	None
What is more, it will lead to perverting the objectives of the special constitutional provisions since the forwards among the backward classes will thereby be enabled to lap up all the special benefits to the exclusion and at the cost of the rest in those classes, thus keeping the rest in perpetual backwardness.	None
The object of the special constitutional provisions is not to uplift a few individuals and families in the backward classes but to ensure the advancement of the backward classes as a whole.	None
Hence, taking out the forwards from among the backward classes is not only permissible but obligatory under the Constitution.	None
However, it is necessary to add that just as the backwardness of the backward groups cannot be measured in terms of the forwardness of the forward groups, so also the forwardness of the forwards among the backward classes cannot be measured in terms of the backwardness of the backward sections of the said classes.	None
It has to be judged on the basis of the social capacities gained by them to compete with the forward classes.	None
So long as the individuals belonging to the backward classes do not develop sufficient capacities of their own to compete with others, they can hardly be classified as forward.	None
xx	None
xx	None
xx	None
More backward and backward is an illusion.	None
No constitutional exercise is called for it.	None
What is required is practical approach to the problem.	None
The collectivity or the group may be backward class but the individuals from that class may have achieved the social status or economic affluence.	None
Disentitle them from claiming reservation.	None
Therefore, while reserving posts for backward classes, the departments should make a condition precedent that every candidate must disclose the annual income of the parents beyond which one could not be considered to be backward.	None
What should be that limit can be determined by the appropriate State.	None
Income apart, provision should be made that wards of those backward classes of persons who have achieved a particular status in society either political or social or economic or if their parents are in higher services then such individuals should be precluded to avoid monopolisation of the services reserved for backward classes by a few.	None
Creamy layer, thus, shall stand eliminated.	None
And once a group or collectivity itself is found to have achieved the constitutional objective then it should be excluded from the list of backward class.	None
Therefore, No reservation can be made on economic criteria.	None
It may be under Article 16(4) if such class satisfies the test of inadequate representation.	None
Exclusion of creamy layer is a social purpose.	None
Any legislative or executive action to remove such persons individually or collectively cannot be constitutionally invalid.	None
Xx xx	None
xx	None
Meanstest in this discussion signifies imposition of an income limit, for the purpose of excluding persons (from the backward class) whose income is above the said limit.	None
This submission is very often referred to as the creamy layer argument.	None
Petitioners submit that some members of the designated backward classes are highly advanced socially as well as economically and educationally.	None
It is submitted that they constitute the forward section of that particular backward class as forward as any other forward class member and that they are lapping up all the benefits of reservations meant for that class, without allowing the benefits to reach the truly backward members of that class.	None
These persons are by no means backward and with them a class cannot be treated as backward.	None
It is pointed out that since Jayasree almost every decision has accepted the validity of this submission.	None
On the other hand, the learned counsel for the States of Bihar, Tamil Nadu, Kerala and other counsel for respondents strongly oppose any such distinction.	None
It is submitted that once a class is identified as a backward class after applying the relevant criteria including the economic one, it is not permissible to apply the economic criteria once again and subdivide a backward class into two subcategories.	None
Counsel for the State of Tamil Nadu submitted further that at one stage (in July 1979) the State o f Tamil Nadu did indeed prescribe such an income limit but had to delete it in view of the practical difficulties encountered and also in view of the representations received.	None
In this behalf, the learned counsel invited our attention to Chapter 7H (pages 60 to 62) of the Ambashankar Commission (Tamil Nadu Second Backward Classes Commission) Report.	None
According to the respondents the argument of creamy layer is but a mere ruse, a trick, to deprive the ackward classes of the benefit of reservations.	None
It is submitted that no member of backward class has come forward with this plea and that it ill becomes the members of forward classes to raise this point.	None
Strong reliance is placed upon the observations of Chinnappa Reddy, J in Vasanth kumar to the following effect (SCC p.763, para 72)	None
One must, however, enter a caveat to the criticism that the benefits of reservation are often snatched away by the top creamy layer of backward class or caste.	None
That a few of the seats and posts reserved for backward classes are snatched away by the more fortunate among them is not to say that reservation is not necessary.	None
This is bound to happen in a competitive society such as ours.	None
Are not the unreserved seats and posts snatched away, in the same way, by the top creamy layer of society itself?	None
Seats reserved for the backward classes are taken away by the top layers amongst them on the same principle of merit on which the unreserved seats are taken away by the top layers of society.	None
How can it be bad if reserved seats and posts are snatched away by the creamy layer of backward classes, if such snatching away of unreserved posts by the top creamy layer of society itself is not bad?	None
In our opinion, it is not a question of permissibility or desirability of such test but one of proper and more appropriate identification of a class a backward class.	None
The very concept of a class denotes a number of persons having certain common traits which distinguish them from the others.	None
In a backward class under clause (4) of Article 16, if the connecting link is the social backwardness, it should broadly be the same in a given class.	None
If some of the members are far too advanced socially (which in the context, necessarily means economically and, may also mean educationally) the connecting thread between them and the remaining class snaps.	None
They would be misfits in the class.	None
After excluding them alone, would the class be a compact class.	None
In fact, such exclusion benefits the truly backward.	None
Difficulty, however, really lies in drawing the line how and where to draw the line?	None
For, while drawing the line, it should be ensured that it does not result in taking away with one hand what is given by the other.	None
The basis of exclusion should not merely be economic, unless, of course, the economic advancement is so high that it necessarily means social advancement.	None
Let us illustrate the point.	None
A member of backward class, say a member of carpenter caste, goes to Middle East and works there as a carpenter.	None
If you take his annual income in rupees, it would be fairly high from the Indian standard.	None
Is he to be excluded from the Backward Class?	None
Are his children in India to be deprived of the benefit of Article 16(4)?	None
Situation may, however, be different, if he rises so high economically as to become say a factory owner himself.	None
In such a situation, his social status also rises.	None
He himself would be in a position to provide employment to others.	None
In such a case, his income is merely a measure of his social status.	None
Even otherwise there are several practical difficulties too in imposing an income ceiling.	None
For example, annual income of Rs.36,000 may not count for much in a city like Bombay, Delhi or Calcutta whereas it may be a handsome income in rural India anywhere.	None
The line to be drawn must be a realistic one.	None
Another question would be, should such a line be uniform for the entire country or a given State or should it differ from rural to urban areas and so on.	None
Further, income from agriculture may be difficult to assess and, therefore, in the case of agriculturists, the line may have to be drawn with reference to the extent of holding.	None
While the income of a person can be taken as a measure of his social advancement, the limit to be prescribed should not be such as to result in taking away with one hand what is given with the other.	None
The income limit must be such as to mean and signify social advancement.	None
At the same time, it must be recognised that there are certain positions, the occupants of which can be treated as socially advanced without any further enquiry.	None
For example, if a member of a designated backward class becomes a member of IAS or IPS or any other All India Service, his status is society (social status) rises he is no longer socially disadvantaged.	None
His children get full opportunity to realize their potential.	None
They are in no way handicapped in the race of life.	None
Keeping in mind all these considerations, we direct the Government of India to specify the basis of exclusion whether on the basis of income, extent of holding or otherwise of creamy layer.	None
This shall be done as early as possible, but not exceeding four months.	None
On such specification persons falling within the net of exclusionary rule shall cease to be the members of the Other Backward Classes (covered by the expression backward class of citizens) for the purpose of Article 16(4).	None
The impugned Office Memorandums dated August 13, 1990 and September 25, 1991 shall be implemented subject only to such specification and exclusion of socially advanced persons from the backward classes contemplated by the said O.M.	None
In other words, after the expiry of four months from today, the implementation of the said O.M. shall be subject to the exclusion of the creamy layer in accordance with the criteria to be specified by the Government of India and not otherwise.	None
In Indra Sawhney v. Union of India (1996) 6 SCC 506 ) at page 508)	None
it was noted as follows Thereafter the matter again came up before the Court on 2031995.	None
Finding that the State of Kerala has not taken any steps, this Court issued notice to show cause why action should not be taken for noncompliance of this Courts order.	None
Again the matter came up on 1071995.	None
Even on that date no report of compliance was submitted to the Court instead an affidavit sworn to by the Chief Secretary to the State was handed over explaining the circumstances why the implementation of the judgment was delayed.	None
xx	None
xx	None
xx	None
In the circumstances, out of sheer exhaustion and having regard to the fact that the constitutionality of the Kerala Act 16 of 1995 is pending disposal before this Court, we have decided to get the information ourselves regarding creamy layer issue through a High Level Committee.	None
Accordingly, we request the learned Chief Justice of the Kerala High Court to appoint a retired Judge of the High Court to be the Chairman of the High Level Committee who will induct not more than 4 members from various walks of life to identify the creamy layer among the designated other backward classes in Kerala State in the light of the ruling of this Court in Mandal case and forward the report to this Court within 3 months from the date of receipt of this order.	None
In Indra Sawhney No. 2 it was observed as follows 7.	None
Our Constitution is wedded to the concept of equality and equality is a basic feature.	None
Under Article 15(2), there is a prohibition that the State shall not discriminate against any citizen on the grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex and place of birth or any of them.	None
It is equally true that ours is a casteridden society.	None
Still, it is a constitutional mandate not to discriminate on the basis of caste alone.	None
Provisions can be made for the upliftment of socially and educationally backward classes, Scheduled Castes or Scheduled Tribes or for women and children.	None
Article 16(4) empowers the States for making any provision for reservation in appointments or posts in favour of any backward class of citizens which, in the opinion of the State, is not adequately represented in the services under the State.	None
Reservation is permissible (i) in favour of any backward class of citizens and (ii) if it is not adequately represented in services under the State.	None
Caste only cannot be the basis for reservation.	None
Reservation can be for a backward class citizen of a particular caste.	None
Therefore, from that caste, the creamy layer and the nonbackward class of citizens are to be excluded.	None
If the caste is to be taken into consideration then for finding out the socially and economically backward class, the creamy layer of the caste is to be eliminated for granting benefit of reservation, because that creamy layer cannot be termed as socially and economically backward.	None
These questions are exhaustively dealt with by a nineJudge Bench of this Court in Indra Sawhney v. Union of India and it has been specially held that only caste cannot be the basis for reservation.	None
Inclusion of castes in the list of backward classes cannot be mechanical and cannot be done without adequate relevant data.	None
Nor can it be done for extraneous reasons Likewise, periodic examination of a backward class could lead to its exclusion if it ceases to be socially backward or if it is adequately represented in the services.	None
Once backward, always backward is not acceptable.	None
In any case, the creamy layer has no place in the reservation system.	None
If forward classes are mechanically included in the list of backward classes or if the creamy layer among backward classes is not excluded, then the benefits of reservation will not reach the really backward among the backward classes.	None
Most of the benefits will then be knocked away by the forward castes and the creamy layer.	None
That will leave the truly backward, backward forever.	None
xx	None
xx	None
xx	None
In Indra Sawhney on the question of exclusion of the creamy layer from the backward classes, there was agreement among eight out of the nine learned Judges of this Court.	None
There were five separate judgments in this behalf which required the creamy layer to be identified and excluded.	None
xx xx	None
xx	None
As appears from the judgments of six out of the eight Judges, viz.	None
Jeevan Reddy (for himself and three others), Sawant and Sahai, JJ.	None
(i.e. six learned Judges out of nine), they specifically refer to those in higher services like IAS, IPS and All India Services or near about as persons who have reached a higher level of social advancement and economic status and therefore as a matter of law, such persons are declared not entitled to be treated as backward.	None
They are to be treated as creamy layer without further inquiry.	None
Likewise, persons living in sufficient affluence who are able to provide employment to others are to be treated as having reached a higher social status on account of their affluence, and therefore outside the backward class.	None
Those holding higher levels of agricultural landholdings or getting income from property, beyond a limit, have to be excluded from the backward classes.	None
This, in our opinion, is a judicial declaration made by this Court.	None
Xx xx	None
xx	None
As the creamy layer in the backward class is to be treated on a par with the forward classes and is not entitled to benefits of reservation, it is obvious that if the creamy layer is not excluded, there will be discrimination and violation of Articles 14 and 16(1) inasmuch as equals (forwards and creamy layer of backward classes) cannot be treated unequally .	None
Again, nonexclusion of creamy layer will also be violative of Articles 14, 16(1) and 16(4) of the Constitution of India since unequals (the creamy layer) cannot be treated as equals , that is to say, equal to the rest of the backward class.	Arguments of Petitioner
These twin aspects of discrimination are specifically elucidated in the judgment of Sawant, J. where the learned Judge stated as follows (SCC p. 553, para 520) To continue to confer upon such advanced sections special benefits, would amount to treating equals unequally.	None
Secondly, to rank them with the rest of the backward classes would amount to treating the unequals equally.	None
Thus, any executive or legislative action refusing to exclude the creamy layer from the benefits of reservation will be violative of Articles 14 and 16(1) and also of Article 16(4).	None
We shall examine the validity of Sections 3, 4 and 6 in the light of the above principle.	None
Xx xx xx	None
The Preamble to the Constitution of India emphasises the principle of equality as basic to our Constitution.	None
In Kesavananda Bharati v. State of Kerala it was ruled that even constitutional amendments which offended the basic structure of the Constitution would be ultra vires the basic structure.	None
Sikri, C.J. laid stress on the basic features enumerated in the Preamble to the Constitution and said that there were other basic features too which could be gathered from the constitutional scheme (para 506A of SCC).	None
Equality was one of the basic features referred to in the Preamble to our Constitution.	None
Shelat and Grover, JJ. also referred to the basic rights referred to in the Preamble.	None
They specifically referred to equality (paras 520 and 535A of SCC).	None
Hegde and Shelat, JJ.	None
also referred to the Preamble (paras 648, 652).	None
Ray, J. (as he then was) also did so (para 886).	None
Jaganmohan Reddy, J. too referred to the Preamble and the equality doctrine (para 1159).	None
Khanna, J. accepted this position (para 1471).	None
Mathew, J. referred to equality as a basic feature (para 1621).	None
Dwivedi, J. (paras 1882, 1883) and Chandrachud, J. (as he then was) (see para 2086) accepted this position.	None
What we mean to say is that Parliament and the legislature in this country cannot transgress the basic feature of the Constitution, namely, the principle of equality enshrined in Article 14 of which Article 16(1) is a facet.	None
Whether the creamy layer is not excluded or whether forward castes get included in the list of backward classes , the position will be the same, namely, that there will be a breach not only of Article 14 but of the basic structure of the Constitution.	None
The nonexclusion of the creamy layer or the inclusion of forward castes in the list of backward classes will, therefore, be totally illegal.	None
Such an illegality offending the root of the Constitution of India cannot be allowed to be perpetuated even by constitutional amendment.	None
The Kerala Legislature is, therefore, least competent to perpetuate such an illegal discrimination.	None
What even Parliament cannot do, the Kerala Legislature cannot achieve.	None
Though in M. Nagarajs case (supra) some observations of general nature have been made so far as the applicability of the principles to Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes are concerned, really that case did not concern with Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes.	None
Similar is the position here.	None
The focus on the identity test in M. Nagarajs case (supra) is unexceptionable.	None
At paras 80 and 110, it was noted as follows Before concluding, we may refer to the judgment of this Court in M.G. Badappanavar.	None
In that case the facts were as follows.	None
Appellants were general candidates.	None
They contended that when they and the reserved candidates were appointed at Level1 and junior reserved candidates got promoted earlier on the basis of roster points to Level2 and again by way of rosterpoints to Level3, and when the senior general candidate got promoted to Level3, then the general candidate would become senior to the reserved candidate at Level3.	None
At Level3, the reserved candidate should have been considered along with the senior general candidate for promotion to Level4.	None
In support of their contention, appellants relied upon the judgment of the Constitution Bench in Ajit Singh (II).	None
The above contentions raised by the appellants were rejected by the tribunal.	None
Therefore, the general candidates came to this Court in appeal.	None
This Court found on facts that the Service Rule concerned did not contemplate computation of seniority in respect of roster promotions.	None
Placing reliance on the judgment of this Court in Ajit Singh (I) and in Virpal Singh, this Court held that roster promotions were meant only for the limited purpose of due representation of backward classes at various levels of service and, therefore, such roster promotions did not confer consequential seniority to the rosterpoint promotee.	None
In Ajit Singh (II) , the circular which gave seniority to the rosterpoint promotees was held to be violative of Articles 14 and 16.	None
It was further held in M.G. Badappanavar that equality is the basic feature of the Constitution and any treatment of equals as unequals or any treatment of unequals as equals violated the basic structure of the Constitution.	None
For this proposition, this Court placed reliance on the judgment in Indra Sawhney while holding that if creamy layer among backward classes were given some benefits as backward classes, it will amount to equals being treated unequals.	None
Applying the creamy layer test, this Court held that if rosterpoint promotees are given consequential seniority, it will violate the equality principle which is part of the basic structure of the Constitution and in which event, even Article 16(4A) cannot be of any help to the reserved category candidates.	None
This is the only judgment of this Court delivered by threeJudge bench saying that if rosterpoint promotees are given the benefit of consequential seniority, it will result in violation of equality principle which is part of the basic structure of the Constitution.	None
Accordingly, the judgment of the tribunal was set aside.	None
xx xx	None
xx	None
As stated above, the boundaries of the width of the power, namely, the ceilinglimit of 50 (the numerical benchmark), the principle of creamy layer, the compelling reasons, namely, backwardness, inadequacy of representation and the overall administrative efficiency are not obliterated by the impugned amendments.	None
At the appropriate time, we have to consider the law as enacted by various States providing for reservation if challenged.	None
At that time we have to see whether limitations on the exercise of power are violated.	None
The State is free to exercise its discretion of providing for reservation subject to limitation, namely, that there must exist compelling reasons of backwardness, inadequacy of representation in a class of post(s) keeping in mind the overall administrative efficiency.	None
It is made clear that even if the State has reasons to make reservation, as stated above, if the impugned law violates any of the above substantive limits on the width of the power the same would be liable to be set aside.	None
There is an interesting article by an author dealing with Affirmative Action which reads as follows In his much referred to speech on 26 November 1949, Dr. Ambedkar said that India was wanting in its recognition of the principle of fraternity.	None
What does fraternity mean?	None
Fraternity means a sense of common brotherhood of all Indians  of India being one people.	None
The virtues of liberty by themselves do not create fraternity.	None
This is why several liberal theorists are unsure about whether or not state interventions should be allowed for when the issue of overcoming disprivileges are concerned.	None
The central concern then is how to inculcate a sense of common brotherhood among people with divergent histories and who occupy vastly different positions in the economic and social structure of a society.	None
Before we go further on discussing the specifics of caste and reservations in India it is worth recording that liberty and equality can sometimes be contradictorily positioned.	None
This is why it is important for democracy to redress these communitybased grievances within a framework that does not violate liberal principles.	None
While the individual needs to be protected, there are individuals in certain groups and communities that need safeguards and support as well.	None
After all it must be remembered that communities do not create citizens, but that there are citizens within communities.	None
Also, while it is rather risky to say that communities have rights, there is no doubt at all that within liberal democracies, individuals have rights.	None
Indeed, these rights were secured historically so that individuals did not have to be burdened by community and ascriptive pressures on them.	None
The rationale behind affirmative action is that it releases suppressed talents and expands the pool of social assets in society for the general good.	None
If today we are looking for a justification for affirmative action in this fashion, several decades ago it was precisely this enlarging of the social pool of talents that recommended equal treatment for women.	None
As L.T. Hobhouse argued then that when women are repressed then there is a loss of all the elements in the common stock which the free play of the womans mind would contribute.	None
By increasing the sum of realized talents in society individuals can actually gain greater intersubjectivity in their everyday lives.	None
As the set of resemblances between them is now so much larger, they can practice, pace Rawls, the moral precept of participating in one anothers fate.	None
In this process, fraternal values of citizenship gain materiality and fulfilment.	None
It should be recognized that fraternity can only come about through a basic set of resemblances between citizens.	None
This conception of resemblances is about citizens being equally able to avail of institutional facilities that ensure their acquisition of those skills that are considered to be socially valuable.	None
In other words, social opportunities exist for individual selfexpansion, and it is only individuals now who can exclude themselves.	None
If grinding poverty comes in the way of acquiring such socially valuable skills, then those blocks should be met by developmental interventions such as the antipoverty programmes.	None
But on no account should the removal of poverty be made synonymous with reservations.	None
Reservations are only meant to create a measure of confidence and dignity among those who didnt dare dream of an alternative life.	None
But that alone cannot create structural conditions that address the root causes of poverty.	None
If quality education and the imparting of socially valuable skills are provided across the board through reservations, then that would take care of the complaint that affirmative action is largely about the equality of results.	None
Rawls principle of justice as fairness only says that offices should be open to all.	None
But what if people do not qualify for these offices because their potentialities have remained unrealized on account of inadequate qualifications arising from a history of discrimination compounded by poverty, or, indeed, because of substandard education?	None
Does it mean that, through positive discrimination and reservations, they should be given these jobs anyway regardless of the welfare of institutions?	None
In this connection, Andre Beteilles warning that affirmative action should be sensitive to institutional wellbeing as well needs to be recalled.	None
Beteille sifted between the various imperatives that different organizations are subsumed under and accordingly advised a careful calibration of reservations such that these provisions of performance do not undermine efficiency of performance.	None
The resemblances that are being advocated in the context of affirmative action should not be interpreted in terms of homogeneous sameness.	None
Sameness is what medieval religious fundamentalists aim for.	None
On the other hand, the set of resemblances in a constitutional democracy enhances equality and not sameness by providing identical opportunities to all for selfexpression and development.	None
Citizenship is not about the sameness of lifestyles or of income.	None
Marshalls notion of citizenship as a status that tends towards equality should be interpreted in this light.	None
According to Marshall, the equality that citizenship guarantees should be the foundation on which other kinds of differences can develop.	None
It will no doubt be the case that differences will exist even after a minimum set of resemblances is established.	None
But these will no longer be outcomes of the accidents of birth.	None
When diversity exists outside of choice then that is not a state of affairs that a democratic society can rejoice in.	None
Affirmative action is instrumental in enlarging the scope of difference and diversity, but it succeeds in doing so by first ensuring that citizens resemble one another at a very critical level namely in their ability to acquire socially valuable skills.	None
Affirmative action gets somewhat complicated in India on account of caste politics.	None
Undeniably, India is the most stratified society in the world.	None
Over and above caste differentiations there are huge income disparities, religious and community differences that are deeply engraved into everyday social relations.	None
No doubt, the nature of caste and community interactions has changed over time, but considerations along ascriptive lines still remain important markers, both at the public and private domains.	None
Not only are we now confronted by identity assertions of earthy peasant castes, that were earlier ranked as lowly shudras (or menials), but also, of those who, till recently, were called untouchables.	None
Now we also know that none of these castes had ever ideologically accepted their degraded status.	None
Yet they lived out their humble lives quietly for generations for fear of offending the privileged strata.	None
We now know more of their origin tales that boast of the elevated positions they once held before an unsuspected chicanery, a lost war, or a mercurial god, demoted them to lowly rungs in popular perceptions.	None
Today these tales are an important source of symbolic energy for caste mobilizations and identity assertions.	None
Now that the Mandal recommendations are in place, reservations are not just for the Scheduled Castes and Tribes, but for the socalled other Backward Castes as well.	None
While there are a large number of castes listed as Backward, the demand for reservations for this category has been spearheaded by the class of ownercultivators, or peasant proprietors.	None
Before we assess Mandal reforms it would be useful to know how these peasant castes emerged.	None
After the zamindari abolition came into effect, adult franchise and landtothetiller programme together forced the earlier landed castes slowly to cede ground in the villages.	None
Soon, however, traditional peasant castes such as the Ahirs, Kurmis, Koeris, Lodhs, Rajputs and Jats began to dominate the political scape of northern India.	None
In the southern State of Tamil Nadu, the Vanniyars and Thevars have become assertive, and in Karnataka control was wrested in the mid1950s from the traditional rural elite within the Congress Party by the Vokkaligas and Linagayats.	None
xx	None
xx	None
xx	None
In pursuance of Article 340 of the Constitution, the Kalelkar Commission was set up in 1955 but it could not come to any satisfactory conclusion about who should be legitimately considered as OBCs.	None
The Mandal Commission came into existence in 1980 and it promptly came up with a long list of 3,743 backward castes on the basis of social, economic and educational backwardness.	None
The Mandal Commissions recommendations were implemented in 1990 by the then Prime Minister VP Singh.	None
This meant that a further 29 per cent of seats in educational institutions and government jobs would now be reserved for OBCs.	None
The implementation of reservations for OBCs set off a furore of protests, including a few suicides, all over the country by those who are considered to be members of forward castes.	None
Many felt that reservations for OBCs were not warranted for two reasons.	None
First, this would make India a caste society by law and, second, because many of those who are considered as OBCs are really quite powerful and dominant in rural India.	None
The obvious reference was to Jats and Yadavs.	None
A majority of social anthropologists wrote against reservations for OBCs primarily on these grounds.	None
Andre Beteilles criticism of the Mandal Commission recommendations was widely commented upon.	None
He distinguishes between reservations for OBCs following Mandal recommendations and the reservations that were already granted in the Constitution for Scheduled Castes and Tribes.	None
While provisions for Scheduled Castes and Tribes were with the intention of reaching towards greater equality, reservations for OBCs were really to bring about a balance of power on the calculus of caste.	None
The kind of deprivations that exuntouchables (Scheduled Castes) and Adivasis (Scheduled Tribes) encountered for centuries can in no way be compared to the traditional condition of the OBCs.	None
Besides, many OBCs are quite powerful in rural India, both economically and politically.	None
In fact, the Mandal Commission recommendations were actually giving in to a powerful rural lobby that did not really care for equality of opportunities as much as it did for equality of results.	None
xx xx	None
xx	None
There are two considerations that escape many uncritical applications of affirmative action.	None
First, affirmative action must resist any tendency whereby its beneficiaries become vested interests.	None
And secondly, it must eventually seek its own dissolution.	None
While the second may be far away, it is by paying attention to the first issue that it is possible for affirmative action to eventually annihilate itself.	None
Paradoxical as it may appear, but when this happens it is then that positive discrimination has finally triumphed.	None
Affirmative action fails to reach this final destination when it is inconsistently applied, or when its beneficiaries form vested interest bloc within a democratic electoral system on the basis of ascriptive identity alone.	None
The latter poses a stronger practical and intellectual challenge to the policy of affirmative action.	None
As long as historical disprivileges and economic backwardness go together and the relationship between them is statistically very strong, colour or caste membership can act as ready reckoners for targeting beneficiaries of affirmative action.	None
This, however, does not mean that membership in these communities should advantage individuals in perpetuity once they are able to develop the minimum set of resemblances.	None
Therefore, as and when those who belong to targeted categories for affirmative action acquire socially useful talents and attributes, they should contribute them to the society as a whole, and not employ them only for sectional advantages.	None
Consequently, those who benefit from this policy owe it to society to put their newly acquired social talents back into the collective social pool.	None
This would mean that they would automatically fall outside the scope of affirmative action programme in the future.	None
The net would no longer cover them as they already have socially useful assets.	None
Indeed the society will be richer and better endowed on account of it as the beneficiaries of affirmative action will now begin to contribute to the social pool of talents.	None
This would both release and add to social and material resources required for continuing with the policy aimed at the enhancement of resemblances.	None
As a result, society will progressively acquire a higher strike rate with the policy of affirmative action by reaching out to those who have thus far fallen outside its ambit.	None
By increasing the number of those who possess the minimum set of resemblances, the society has now a larger wealth of talents in a variety of fields and specialities than it had before.	None
This is how affirmative action, which is aimed at the historically most disadvantaged sections, ultimately improves the lot of everybody in society.	None
If, on the other hand, either colour or race, which are only ready reckoners, become permanent considerations, without taking into account biographical profiles of actual and potential beneficiaries, then that would inhibit fraternity and sow seeds of permanent divisions in society.	None
Affirmative action begins by placing the assets of the better off in a collective pool, not for redistribution, but to create the infrastructure that is needed to enhance the minimum set of resemblances necessary for substantive citizenship.	None
With the help of this capital, socially valuable assets are now created in sites where there were none.	None
This measure has a strong practical dimension for out of this collective pooling new assets are being created.	None
The creation of such new assets is possible because the initial pooling of assets of the privileged section allows the society to underwrite the expenses incurred for the establishment of certain baseline similarities in society as a whole.	None
As the most important feature in this case is not ones ascriptive badge, but the creation of socially valuable assets, it is expected that those who have been the beneficiaries of the scheme will gradually slip out of the net.	None
They will cease to receive from the collective pool and instead will begin to contribute to it.	None
As far as public policy is concerned they are no long members of certain designated castes or communities.	None
They are now simply citizens.	None
In passing it is worth putting in perspective that the difference between reservations in India and affirmative action in America is that the former talks about extirpating caste whereas the latter is interested primarily in representing races.	None
If the accent is on representation then the ascriptive factor becomes a permanent badge that can never be overcome.	None
Again, Americans believe in race representation, not in quotas, and in not sacrificing standards for social justice.	None
But the great similarity between the two forms of preferential policy is that in both cases it is the public sector where positive discrimination is effectively realized.	None
In America, the State encourages private sector units to employ people of diverse backgrounds without specifying quotas for different races.	None
If these enterprises can show a fair racial mix then they can get preferential contracts from the government.	None
The State cannot force any private sector unit to implement affirmative action.	None
It is a combination of goodwill and rewards that takes affirmative action forward in the private sector of America.	None
For example, Bob Jones University does not receive any public money and, therefore, it refuses to accept affirmative action, even of the most muted kind.	None
It is only when organizations depend on state funding, or when they want to be rewarded by the State, that policy of affirmative action comes to life.	None
It has been rightly observed in Indra Sawhney No. 2 (supra) whether creamy layer is not excluded or whether forward classes can be excluded in the list of backward classes, the position would be the same and there will be breach not only of Article 14 but of the basic structure of the Constitution.	None
As was rightly observed in the said case, non exclusion of the creamy layer or inclusion of forward castes in the lists of backward classes will be totally illegal.	None
The illegality offends the roots and foundation of the Constitution and cannot be allowed to be perpetuated.	None
In Nair Service Societys case (supra) this Court observed as follows This Court, thus, has categorically laid down the law that determination of creamy layer is a part of the constitutional scheme.	None
In our view, even non exclusion of the creamy layer for the purpose of admission to the educational institutions cannot be countenanced.	None
It is inconceivable that a person who belongs to the creamy layer is socially and educationally backward.	None
The backward status vanishes when somebody becomes part of the creamy layer.	None
In Vasant Kumars case (supra) it was aptly described that the benefits of reservation are snatched away by the top creamy layer of the backward classes and this has to be avoided at any cost.	None
By inclusion of the creamy layer or in other words non inclusion thereof a fresh lease of life to those who should have been left out is given.	None
Their continuance would mean keeping weakest amongst the weak always weak and leaving the fortunate ones to enjoy the benefits.	None
If the ultimate aim is a casteless and classless society in line with the dream of the Constitution framers that has to be chewed out.	None
As Father of the Nation had once said if the caste system as we know is an anchronism, then it must go.	None
There is a feeling and it cannot be said without reason that reservation hits at the root of this belief and instead of its obliteration there is perceivable perpetuation.	None
It is true that obliteration cannot be done immediately or within a short span of time but that is no answer to the lack of seriousness in seeking obliteration.	None
In Indra Sawhney No.1 (supra) the following observations on the question of giving priority over reservation are of significance.	None
It was held Preference without reservation may be adopted in favour of the chosen classes of citizens by prescribing for them a longer period for passing a test or by awarding additional marks or granting other advantages like relaxation of age or other minimum requirements.	None
(See the preferential treatment in State of Kerala and Anr.	None
v. N.M.	None
Thomas and Ors.	None
(1976) 1	None
SCR 906 ).	None
Furthermore, it would be within the discretion of the State to provide financial assistance to such persons by way of grant, scholarships, fee concessions etc.	None
Such preferences or advantages are like temporary crutches for additional support to enable the members of the backward and other disadvantaged classes to march forward and compete with the rest of the people.	None
These preferences are extended to them because of their inability otherwise to compete effectively in open selections on the basis of merits for appointment to posts in public services and the like or for selection to academic courses.	None
Such preferences can be extended to all disadvantaged classes of citizens, whether or not they are victims of prior discrimination.	None
What qualifies persons for preference is backwardness or disadvantage of any kind which the State has a responsibility to ameliorate.	None
The blind and the deaf, the dumb and the maimed, and other handicapped persons qualify for preference.	None
So do all other classes of citizens who are at a comparative disadvantage for whatever reason, and whether or not they are victims of prior discrimination.	None
All these persons may be beneficiaries of preferences short of reservation.	None
Any such preference, although discriminatory on its face, may be justified as a benign classification for affirmative action warranted by a compelling state interest.294.	None
In addition to such preferences, quotas may be provided exclusively reserving posts in public services or seats in academic institutions for backward people entitled to such protection.	None
Reservation is intended to redress backwardness of a higher degree.	None
Reservation prima facie is the very antithesis of a free and open selection.	None
It is a discriminatory exclusion of the disfavoured classes of meritorious candidates M.R. Balaji (supra).	None
It is not a case of merely providing an advantage or a concession or preference in favour of the backward classes and other disadvantaged groups.	None
It is not even a handicap to disadvantage the forward classes so as to attain a measure of qualitative or relative equality between the two groups.	None
Reservation which excludes from consideration all those persons falling outside the specially favoured groups, irrespective of merits and qualifications, is much more positive and drastic a discrimination  albeit to achieve the same end of qualitative equality  but unless strictly and narrowly tailored to a compelling constitutional mandate, it is unlikely to qualify as a benign discrimination.	None
Unlike in the case of other affirmative action programmes, backwardness by itself is not sufficient to warrant reservation.	None
What qualifies for reservation is backwardness which is the result of identified past discrimination and which is comparable to that of the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes.	None
Reservation is a remedial action specially addressed to the ill effects stemming from historical discrimination.	None
To ignore this vital distinction between affirmative action short of reservation and reservation by a predetermined quota as a remedy for past inequities is to ignore the special characteristic of the constitutional grant of power specially addressed to the constitutionally recognised backwardness.	None
xx xx	None
xx	None
Reservation should be avoided except in extreme cases of acute backwardness resulting from prior discrimination as in the case of the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes and other classes of persons in comparable positions.	None
In all other cases, preferential treatment short of reservation can be adopted.	None
Any such action, though in some respects discriminatory, is permissible on the basis of a legitimate classification rationally related to the attainment of equality in all its aspects.	None
