It has hampered its growth.	None
To have a casteless society will be realization of a noble dream.	None
To start with, the effect of reservation may appear to perpetuate caste.	None
The immediate effect of caste based reservation has been rather unfortunate.	None
In the prereservation era people wanted to get rid of the backward tag  either social or economical.	None
But post reservation, there is a tendency even among those who are considered as forward, to seek backward tag, in the hope of enjoying the benefits of reservations.	None
When more and more people aspire for backwardness instead of forwardness the country itself stagnates.	None
Be that as it may.	None
Reservation as an affirmative action is required only for a limited period to bring forward the socially and educationally backward classes by giving them a gentle supportive push.	None
But if there is no review after a reasonable period and if reservation is continued, the country will become a caste divided society permanently.	None
Instead of developing an united society with diversity, we will end up as a fractured society for ever suspicious of each other.	None
While affirmative discrimination is a road to equality, care should be taken that the road does not become a rut in which the vehicle of progress gets entrenched and stuck.	None
Any provision for reservation is a temporary crutch.	None
Such crutch by unnecessary prolonged use, should not become a permanent liability.	None
It is significant that Constitution does not specifically prescribe a casteless society nor tries to abolish caste.	None
But by barring discrimination in the name of caste and by providing for affirmative action Constitution seeks to remove the difference in status on the basis of caste.	None
When the differences in status among castes are removed, all castes will become equal.	None
That will be a beginning for a casteless egalitarian society.	None
I agree that the petitions shall stand disposed of in the manner stated by the learned Chief Justice.	None
Dalveer Bhandari, J. The 93rd Amendment to the Constitution directly or indirectly affects millions of citizens of this country.	None
It has been challenged in a number of writ petitions.	None
This Court heard these petitions intermittently over the course of several months.	None
Appearing on behalf of petitioners and respondents, the countrys finest legal minds assisted us.	None
The fundamental question that arises in these writ petitions is Whether Article 15(5), inserted by the 93rd Amendment, is consistent with the other provisions of the Constitution or whether its impact runs contrary to the Constitutional aim of achieving a casteless and classless society?	None
On behalf of the petitioners, Senior Advocate Mr. F.S. Nariman, eloquently argued that if Article 15(5) is permitted to remain in force, then, instead of achieving the goal of a casteless and classless society, India would be converted into a casteridden society.	None
The country would forever remain divided on caste lines.	None
The Government has sought to repudiate this argument.	None
Petitioners argument, however, echoes the grave concern of our Constitutions original Framers.	None
On careful analysis of the Constituent Assembly and the Parliamentary Debates, one thing is crystal clear our leaders have always and unanimously proclaimed with one voice that our constitutional goal is to establish a casteless and classless society.	None
Mahatma Gandhi said The caste system as we know is an anachronism.	None
It must go if both Hinduism and India are to live and grow from day to day.	None
The first Prime Minister, Pt. Jawahar Lal Nehru, said that no one should be left in any doubt that the future Indian Society was to be casteless and classless.	None
Dr. B. R. Ambedkar called caste antinational.	None
After almost four decades of independence, while participating in the Parliamentary Debate on the Mandal issue, then Prime Minister Shri Rajiv Gandhi on 6th September, 1990 again reiterated the same sentiments I think, nobody in this House will say that the removal of casteism is not part of the national goal, therefore, it would be in the larger interest of the nation to get rid of the castes as early as possible.	None
It is our bounden duty and obligation to examine the validity of the 93rd Amendment in the background of the Preamble and the ultimate goal that runs through the pages of the Constitution.	None
To attain an egalitarian society, we have to urgently remove socioeconomic inequalities.	None
All learned counsel for the petitioners asserted that we must deliver the benefits of reservation to only those who really deserve it.	None
This can only be done if we remove the creamy layer.	None
Learned counsel for the Union of India and other respondents opposed this assertion.	None
The principle of creamy layer emanates from the broad doctrine of equality itself.	None
Unless the creamy layer is removed from admissions and service reservation, the benefits would not reach the group in whose name the impugned legislation was passed  the poorest of the poor.	None
Therefore, including the creamy layer would be inherently unjust.	None
Creamy layer exclusion, however, is just one of the many issues raised by the parties.	None
I need to examine various facets of this case in order to decide the validity of the 93rd Amendment and the Central Educational Institutions (Reservation in Admission) Bill, 2006 (passed as Act 5 of 2007) (hereinafter called the Reservation Act).	None
I shall focus my analysis on the following issues 1A. Whether the creamy layer be excluded from the 93rd Amendment (Reservation Act)?	None
1B. What are the parameters for creamy layer exclusion?	None
1C. Is creamy layer exclusion applicable to SC ST?	None
Can the Fundamental Right under Article 21A be accomplished without great emphasis on primary education?	None
Does the 93rd Amendment violate the Basic Structure of the Constitution by imposing reservation on unaided institutions?	None
Whether the use of caste to identify SEBCs runs afoul of the casteless classless society, in violation of Secularism.	None
Are Articles 15(4) and 15(5) mutually contradictory, such that 15(5) is unconstitutional?	None
Does Article 15(5)s exemption of minority institutions from the purview of reservation violate Article 14 of the Constitution?	None
Are the standards of review laid down by the U.S. Supreme Court applicable to our review of affirmative action under Art 15(5) and similar provisions?	None
With respect to OBC identification, was the Reservation Acts delegation of power to the Union Government excessive?	None
Is the impugned legislation invalid as it fails to set a timelimit for castebased reservation?	None
At what point is a student no longer Educationally Backward and thus no longer eligible for special provisions under 15(5)?	None
Would it be reasonable to balance OBC reservation with societal interests by instituting OBC cutoff marks that are slightly lower than that of the general category?	None
I have carefully examined the pleadings and written submissions submitted at length.	None
Admittedly, the provisions of the Constitution and the Preamble lead to the irresistible conclusion that the Nation has always wanted to achieve a casteless and classless society.	None
If we permit this impugned legislation to be implemented, I am afraid, instead of a casteless and classless India, we would be left with a casteridden society.	None
The first place where caste can be eradicated is the classroom.	None
It all starts with education.	None
In other words, if you belong to a lower caste but are well qualified, hardly anyone would care about your caste.	None
Free and compulsory education is now a fundamental right under Article 21A.	None
The State is duty bound to implement this Article on a priority basis.	None
There has been grave laxity in its implementation.	None
This laxity adversely affects almost every walk of life.	None
In my opinion, nothing is more important for the Union of India than to implement this critical Article.	None
I direct the Union of India to set a timelimit within which this Article is going to be completely implemented.	None
This timelimit must be set within six months.	None
In case the Union of India fails to fix the timelimit, then perhaps this work will also have to be done by the Court.	None
The Union of India should appreciate in proper prospective that the root cause of social and educational backwardness is poverty.	None
All efforts have to be made to eradicate this fundamental problem.	None
Unless the creamy layer is removed, the benefit would not reach those who are in need.	None
Reservation sends the wrong message.	None
Everybody is keen to get the benefit of backward class status.	None
If we want to really help the socially, educationally and economically backward classes, we need to earnestly focus on implementing Article 21A.	None
We must provide educational opportunity from day one.	None
Only then will the casteless classless society be within our grasp.	None
Once children are of collegegoing age, it is too late for reservation to have much of an effect.	None
The problem with the Reservation Act is that most of the beneficiaries will belong to the creamy layer, a group for which no benefits are necessary.	None
Only noncreamy layer OBCs can avail of reservations in college admissions, and once they graduate from college they should no longer be eligible for postgraduate reservation.	None
27 is the upper limit for OBC reservation.	None
The Government need not always provide the maximum limit.	None
Reasonable cut off marks should be set so that standards of excellence greatly effect.	None
The unfilled seats should revert to the general category.	None
These issues first arise out of the text of the impugned Amendment.	None
Reservation for Socially and Educationally Backward Classes of Citizens (SEBCs) was introduced by the 93rd Amendment.	None
Article 15(5) states Nothing in this article or in subclause (g) of clause (1) of article 19 shall prevent the State from making any special provision, by law, for the advancement of any socially and educationally backward classes of citizens or for the Scheduled Castes or the Scheduled Tribes in so far as such special provisions relate to their admission to educational institutions including private educational institutions, whether aided or unaided by the State, other than minority educational institutions referred to in clause (1) of article 30.	Reasoning
Excluding the Creamy Layer from receiving special benefits Affirmative action is employed to eliminate substantive social and economic inequality by providing opportunities to those who may not otherwise gain admission or employment.	None
Articles 14, 15 and 16 allow for affirmative action.	None
To promote Article 14 egalitarian equality, the State may classify citizens into groups, giving preferential treatment to one over another.	None
When it classifies, the State must keep those who are unequal out of the same batch to achieve constitutional goal of egalitarian society.	None
Arguments of the Union of India in regard to the creamy layer Mr. G.E. Vahanvati, learned Solicitor General and Mr. K. Parasaran, Senior Advocate appearing for the Government contend that creamy layer exclusion is a bad policy.	None
They argue that if you exclude the creamy layer, there would be a shortage of candidates who can afford to pay for higher education.	None
This argument harms rather than helps the Government.	None
It cannot be seriously disputed that most of the collegegoing OBCs belong to the creamy layer for whom reservations are unnecessary they have the money to attend good schools, tuitions and coaching courses for entrance exams.	None
Naturally, these advantages result in higher test scores visvis the noncreamy layer OBCs.	None
The result is that creamy OBCs would fill the bulk of the OBC quota, leaving the noncreamy no better off than before.	None
If the creamy get most of the benefit, why have reservations in the first place?	None
Learned Senior Counsel for petitioners, Mr. Harish Salve, is justified in arguing that before carrying out Constitutional Amendments the Union of India must clearly target its beneficiaries.	None
He rightly submitted that we should not make law first and thereafter target the laws beneficiaries.	None
Failure to exclude the creamy layer is but one example of this problem.	None
The Government further submitted that the creamy layer should be included to ensure that enough qualified candidates fill 27 of the seats reserved to OBCs.	None
The Oversight Committee disagreed.	None
The Committee relied on data from Karnataka to disprove the contention that seats go unfilled when the creamy is excluded the apprehension that seats will not be filled up if the creamy layer is excluded has been comprehensively shown to be unfounded.	None
See Oversight Committee, Vol. 1, Sept. 2006, p. 69, para 1.7.	None
We shall later review the Oversight Committee opinion in greater detail.	None
The reasons for which the creamy layer should be excluded At the outset, I note that the Parliament rejected the Hindi version of the Reservation Act.	None
The Hindi version of the Reservation Act would have expressly excluded the creamy layer.	None
See Prof.	None
Rasa Singh Rawats comments in the Parliamentary Debate on the Reservation Act, 14 December 2006 The Parliament eventually passed the English version in which the creamy layer is not mentioned, making its intention clear.	None
It wanted to include the creamy layer.	None
For all practical purposes, it did so.	None
Therefore, I will treat it as included.	None
Counsel for the Union of India argued that it is still theoretically possible for the executive to exclude the creamy layer.	None
Much is possible in theory.	None
Given the executives failure to take action since the time the Act was passed, I find this argument unavailing.	None
With the Parliaments intention in view, I will deal in some detail with the reasons as to why the creamy layer should be excluded from reservation.	None
I do so because I want to emphasize that the creamy layer must never be included in any affirmative action legislation.	None
It also becomes imperative to gather the original Framers and the Framers intention.	None
At the outset, we recognise a distinction between the original Framers and the Framers, i.e., Members of the First Parliament.	None
Members of the Constituent Assembly and the First Parliament were one in the same.	None
But the distinction is necessary to the extent that the First Parliament deviated from its constitutional philosophy.	None
By examining the debate on Article 15(4), I may ascertain whether the Framers wanted to exclude the creamy layer.	None
The First Parliament believed that economic was included in the social portion of socially and educationally backward.	None
Prime Minister Nehru said as much One of the main amendments or ideas put forward is in regard to the addition of the word economical.	None
Frankly, the argument put forward, with slight variation, I would accept, but my difficult is this that when we chose those particular words there, for the advancement of any socially and educationally backward classes, we chose them because they occur in article 340 and we wanted to bring them bodily from there.	None
Otherwise I would have had not the slightest objection to add economically.	None
But if I added economically I would at the same time not make it a kind of cumulative thing but would say that a person who is lacking in any of these things should be helped.	None
Socially is a much wider word including many things and certainly including economically.	None
Therefore, I felt that socially and educationally really cover the ground and at the same time you bring out a phrase used in another part of the Constitution in a slightly similar context.	None
(See the Parliamentary Debates on First Amendment Bill, 1 June 1951, p. 9830.)	None
Had it not been for a desire to achieve symmetry in drafting, economically would have been included.	None
Had this been done, the creamy layer would have been excluded ab initio.	None
In the 15(4) debate, Shri M.A. Ayyangars wanted to add economic to ensure that the rich SEBCs would not receive special provisions.	None
I thought economic might be added so that rich men may not take advantage of this provision.	None
In my part of the country there are the Nattukkottai Chettiars who do not care to have English education, but they are the richest of the lot  should there be special reservation for them?	None
(See The Parliamentary Debates on First Amendment Bill, 1 June 1951, p. 9817.)	None
(emphasis added).	None
This hesitation aside, Shri M.A. Ayyangar was satisfied that the term economic was included in the term social.	None
The Framers were worried about creamy layer inclusion, albeit under a different name.	None
They wanted to ensure that the richest of the backward lot would not benefit from special provisions.	None
With their sentiment on our side, we are even more confident that we should strike out in the direction that strikes down laws that include the creamy layer.	None
Including the creamy layer means unequals are treated as equals in violation of the right to equality under Articles 14, 15 and 16.	None
In the present case, Dr. Rajeev Dhavan, the learned Senior Counsel and Mr. S.K. Jain, the learned counsel vehemently argued on behalf of petitioners that it is precisely because equality is at issue that the creamy layer must be removed.	None
The creamy layer has been the subject matter of a number of celebrated judgments of this Court.	None
In a seven Judge Bench in State of Kerala Another v. N. M. Thomas Others (1976) 2 SCC 310 , Justice Mathew, in his concurring judgment, dealt with the right to equality in the following words The guarantee of equality before the law or the equal opportunity in matters of employment is a guarantee of something more than what is required by formal equality.	None
It implies differential treatment of persons who are unequal.	None
Egalitarian principle has therefore enhanced the growing belief that Government has an affirmative duty to eliminate inequalities and to provide opportunities for the exercise of human rights and claims.	None
(emphasis added)	None
In Indra Sawhney Others v. Union of India Others (1992)	None
Supp (3) SCC 217, (hereinafter referred to as Sawhney I), this Court has aptly observed that reservation is given to backward classes until they cease to be backward, and not indefinitely.	None
This Court in para 520 (Sawant, J.) has stated as under Society does not remain static.	None
The industrialisation and the urbanisation which necessarily followed in its wake, the advance on political, social and economic fronts made particularly after the commencement of the Constitution, the social reform movements of the last several decades, the spread of education and the advantages of the special provisions including reservations secured so far, have all undoubtedly seen at least some individuals and families in the backward classes, however small in number, gaining sufficient means to develop their capacities to compete with others in every field.	None
That is an undeniable fact.	None
Legally, therefore, they are not entitled to be any longer called as part of the backward classes whatever their original birthmark.	None
It can further hardly be argued that once a backward class, always a backward class.	None
That would defeat the very purpose of the special provisions made in the Constitution for the advancement of the backward classes, and for enabling them to come to the level of and to compete with the forward classes, as equal citizens.	None
(emphasis supplied).	None
For our purposes, creamy layer OBCs and noncreamy layer OBCs are not equals when it comes to moving up the socioeconomic ladder by means of educational opportunity.	None
Failing to remove the creamy layer treats creamy layer OBCs and noncreamy layer OBCs as equals.	None
In the same paragraph, Justice Sawant stated that to rank the creamy layer with the rest of the backward classes would  amount to treating the unequals equally violating the equality provisions of the Constitution.	None
According to the Kerala Legislature, there was no creamy layer in Kerala.	None
The legislation was challenged in Indra Sawhney v. Union of India Others (2000) 1 SCC 168 , (hereinafter referred to as Sawhney II).	None
The Court struck the two provisions that barred creamy layer exclusion, concluding that noninclusion of the creamylayer and inclusion of forward castes in reservation violates the right to equality under Article 14 and the basic structure.	None
In Sawhney II at para 65, the Court had gone to the extent of observing that not even the Parliament, by constitutional amendment, could dismantle the basic structure by including the creamy layer in reservation What we mean to say is that the Parliament and the legislature in this country cannot transgress the basic feature of the Constitution, namely, the principle of equality enshrined in Article 14 of which Article 16(1) is a facet.	None
Whether the creamy layer is not excluded or whether forward castes get included in the list of backward classes, the position will be the same, namely, that there will be a breach not only of Article 14 but of the basic structure of the Constitution.	None
The nonexclusion of the creamy layer or the inclusion of forward castes in the list of backward classes will, therefore, be totally illegal.	None
Such an illegality offending the root of the Constitution of India cannot be allowed to be perpetuated even by constitutional amendment.	None
By definition, the creamy and noncreamy are unequal when it comes to schooling.	None
Relative to their noncreamy counterparts, the creamy have a distinct advantage in gaining admission.	None
While the creamy and noncreamy are given equal opportunity to gain admission in the reserved category, this equality exists in name only.	None
Will the OBC daughter of a Minister, IAS officer or affluent business owner attend better schools than her noncreamy counterpart?	None
Yes.	None
Will she go to private tuitions unaffordable to her noncreamy counterpart?	None
Certainly.	None
And where will she cram for the alldecisive entrance exams?	None
In a coaching center?	None
Of course.	None
Will she come home from school to find a family member waiting?	None
Probably.	None
And when she seeks help from her parents, are they educated and able to give superior assistance with schoolwork?	None
Most likely.	None
I take judicial notice of these anecdotes, for they flesh out a simple fact she has all the resources that her noncreamy counterpart lacks.	None
It is no surprise that she will outperform the noncreamy.	None
On average, her lot will take the reserved seats.	None
I cannot consider the OBC Ministers daughter and the noncreamy OBC as equals in terms of their chances at earning a university seat nor can I allow them to be treated equally.	None
To lump them in the same category is an unreasonable classification.	None
Putting them in headtohead competition for the same seats violates the right to equality in Articles 14, 15 and 16.	None
In its conclusion at para 122, M. Nagaraj Others v. Union of India Others (2006) 8 SCC 212 , a Constitution Bench of this Court while dealing with Article 16(4A) and 16(4B) with regard to SC and ST observed as under We reiterate that the ceiling limit of 50, the concept of creamy layer and the compelling reasons, namely, backwardness, inadequacy of representation and overall administrative efficiency are all constitutional requirements without which the structure of equality of opportunity in Article 16 would collapse.	None
It was contended that Nagraj is obiter in regard to creamy layer exclusion.	None
According to Nagraj, reservation in promotion for SC ST is contingent on exclusion of the creamy layer.	None
(paras 122, 123 and 124).	None
The contention of the Union of India cannot be accepted.	None
The discussion regarding creamy layer is far from obiter in Nagraj.	None
If the State fails to exclude the SC ST creamy layer, the reservation must fall.	None
Placing this contingency in the conclusion makes the discussion of creamy layer part of the ratio.	None
In sum, creamy layer inclusion violates the right to equality.	None
That is, nonexclusion of creamy layer and inclusion of forward castes in reservation violates the right to equality in Articles 14, 15 and 16 as well as the basic structure of the Constitution.	None
If you belong to the creamy layer, you are not SEBC.	None
One of the prominent questions raised in the writ petitions is whether creamy layer OBCs should be considered socially and educationally backward under the provisions of Article 15(5).	None
While interpreting this provision, a basic syllogism must govern our decision.	None
If you belong to the creamy layer, you are socially advanced and cannot be given the benefit of reservation.	None
(See Sawhney I).	None
Once one is socially advanced, he cannot be socially and educationally backward.	None
He who is socially forward is likely to be educationally forward as well.	None
If either condition (social or educational) goes unmet, one cannot qualify for the benefit of reservation as SEBC.	None
Being socially advanced, the creamy layer is not socially backward pursuant to Articles 15(4) and 15(5) of the Constitution.	None
Even the text of Articles 15(4) and 15(5) provides for creamy layer exclusion.	None
In this sense, one could say that the term creamy layer is synonymous with nonSEBC.	None
Similar interpretation is given to backward classes under Article 16(4).	None
The Parliament could not reasonably make reservation for nonbackwards.	None
Such a Bill on the face of it would violate the Constitution.	None
In Sawhney I, the Government of India issued an O.M. on 13 August 1990, reserving 27 of Government posts to SEBCs.	None
Writing for the majority, at para 792 of page 724, Justice Reddy explained that the creamy layer was not SEBC.	None
The very concept of a class denotes a number of persons having certain common traits which distinguish them from the others.	None
In a backward class under Clause (4) of Article 16, if the connecting link is the social backwardness, it should broadly be the same in a given class.	None
If some of the members are far too advanced socially (which in the context, necessarily means economically and, may also mean educationally) the connecting thread between them and the remaining class snaps.	None
They would be misfits in the class.	None
After excluding them alone, would the class be a compact class.	None
In fact, such exclusion benefits the truly backward.	None
Even though the O.M. was silent on the issue of creamy layer, Justice Reddy excluded the creamy layer at para 859(3)(d).	None
The O.M. could not go into effect until the creamy layer was excluded.	None
para 861(b).	None
Exclusion was only in regard to OBC SC ST were not touched.	None
(para 792).	None
In Sawhney I, the entire discussion was confined only to Other Backward Classes.	None
Similarly, in the instant case, the entire discussion was confined only to Other Backward Classes.	None
Therefore, I express no opinion with regard to the applicability of exclusion of creamy layer to the Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes.	None
Creamy Layer OBCs are not educationally backward In addition to social backwardness, the text of 15(5) demands that recipients are also educationally backward.	None
Even though the creamy layers status as socially advanced is sufficient to disqualify them for preferential treatment, the creamy layer from any community is usually educated and will want the same for its children.	None
They know that education is the key to success.	None
For most, it made them.	None
People belonging to this group do not require reservation.	None
Creamy Layer Inclusion Robs the Poor and Gives to the Rich	None
In a number of judgments, the view has been taken that the creamy layers inclusion takes from the poor and gives to the rich.	None
Our Courts in following cases had taken the same view.	None
See N.M Thomas (supra), para 124 (sevenJudge Bench)	None
K.C.	None
Vasanth Kumar Another v. State of Karnataka, 1985 (Supp) SCC 714, paras 2, 24 and 28 (fiveJudge Bench)	None
Sawhney I., paras 520, 793 and 859(3)(d) (nineJudge Bench)	None
Ashoka Kumar Thakur v. State of Bihar Others (1995) 5 SCC 403 , paras 3, 17 and 18 (twoJudge Bench)	None
Sawhney II,	None
paras 810, 27, 48 and 6566 (threeJudge Bench)	None
Nagaraj (supra), paras, 120124 (fiveJudge Bench)	None
Nair Service Society v. State of Kerala, (2007) 4 SCC 1 paras 31 and 4954 (twoJudge Bench).	None
In Akhil Bharatiya Soshit Karamchari Sangh (Railway) v. Union of India Others (1981) 1 SCC 246 , Justice Iyer had this to say about the creamy layer Maybe, some of the forward lines of the backward classes have the best of both the worlds and their electoral muscle qua caste scares away even radical parties from talking secularism to them.	None
We are not concerned with that dubious brand.	None
In the long run, the recipe for backwardness is not creating a vested interest in backward castes but liquidation of handicaps, social and economic, by constructive projects.	None
All this is in another street and we need not walk that way now.	None
Nor does the specious plea that because a few harijans are better off, therefore, the bulk at the bottom deserves no jackup provisions merit scrutiny.	None
A swallow does not make a summer.	None
Maybe, the State may, when social conditions warrant, justifiably restrict harijan benefits to the harijans among the harijans and forbid the higher harijans from robbing the lowlier brethren.	None
Creamy layer inclusion was not enough to strike an entire provision in this case.	None
He suggests that creamy layer exclusion is an issue to be dealt with at a later time.	None
The argument that there are rich and influential harijans who rob all the privileges leaving the serflevel sufferers as suppressed as ever.	None
The Administration may well innovate and classify to weed out the creamy layer of SCs STs but the court cannot force the State in that behalf.	None
Thus, Justice Iyer does not mandate creamy layer exclusion rather, he leaves the question to the State.	None
Apart from judicial pronouncements, the Oversight Committee suggested that failure to exclude the creamy layer would lead to unfair results.	None
The Committee was cautious to reach a conclusion.	None
In its Report, it stated that the decision taken was to leave the matter to the Government of India, keeping in mind the fact that the creamy layer is not covered in the Reservation Act, 2006.	None
(See Oversight Committee, Vol. 1, p. 33 and 4.2.)	None
Before leaving the matter to the Government, the Committee nevertheless made its recommendation In case it is decided not to exclude the creamy layer, the poorest among the OBCs will be placed at a disadvantage.	None
(emphasis added).	None
(See Oversight Committee at Appendix I in its Report at p. 70, para 1.13).	None
At page 69 of Vol.	None
I of its Report, the Committee offered data to support this conclusion 1.6 Appendix2 examines in detail the status of the socioeconomic development of OBCs in respect of such parameters as relate to poverty, health, education, unemployment, workforce participation, land ownership etc.	None
The analysis of the NSS data clearly brings out that inclusion of the creamy layer will result in reserved seats getting preempted by the OBCs from the top two deciles at the cost of the poorer income deciles of the OBCs.	None
Thus almost all rural OBCs as well as Urban OBCs from the Northern, Central and Eastern regions of India will be deprived of the intended benefits of reservation.	None
emphasis added 1.7 On the other hand, it was argued that if the creamy layer of OBCs is denied access to reservation in education paripassau with the principle applied in the case of employment, the reserved seats may not get filled up, again defeating the purpose of bringing in reservation for the OBCs.	None
In a case study from Karnataka (included in Annexure X), it has been clearly shown that the OBC quotas have been utilized without any compromise with academic excellence in a situation where the creamy layer has been excluded.	None
The apprehension that seats will not be filled up if the creamy layer is excluded has been comprehensively shown to be unfounded.	None
The case study shows that the performance of students from below the creamy layer is outstanding and much better than general category students.	None
The Committee could have played it safe.	None
Despite some opposition, the Committee included its opinion on the matter.	None
And that opinion is unequivocal the creamy must be excluded.	None
What is allegedly for the poor goes to the rich.	None
Is that reasonable?	None
Trumpeted by the Parliament as a boost to the morale of the downtrodden and in the right direction of ensuring social justice to other backward classes and ensuring social justice to those weaker sections, Article 15(5) dupes those who actually need preferential treatment.	None
(See Prof. Basudeb Barman, M.P., the Parliamentary Debates, p. 531, December 21, 2005 Prof. M. Ramadass, M.P., at p. 510 and Shri C.K. Chandrappan, M.P., at p. 494 respectively).	None
For the poorest of the poor, reservation in college is an empty promise.	None
Few of the financially poor OBCs attend high school, let alone college.	None
Instead of rewarding those that complete Plus 2, the 93rd Amendment (Art 15(5)) poses another barrier they will have to compete with the creamy layer for reserved seats.	None
As explained, the poor lack the resources to compete with the creamy, who snatch away those seats.	None
N. M. Thomas (supra), para 124 (Iyer, J.).	None
With the creamy excluded, poor OBCs would compete with poor OBCs the playing field levelled.	None
As it stands, the Amendment and Act serve one purpose they provide a windfall of seats to the rich and powerful amongst the OBCs.	None
It is unreasonable to classify rich and poor OBCs as a single entity.	None
As noted, this violates the Article 14 right to equality.	None
Unless the creamy layer is removed, OBCs cannot exercise their group rights.	None
The Union of India and other respondents argued that creamy layer exclusion is wrong because the text of the 93rd Amendment bestows a benefit on classes, not individuals.	None
While it is a group right, the group must contain only those individuals that belong to the group.	None
I first take the entire lot of creamy and non creamy layer OBCs.	None
I then remove the creamy layer on an individual basis based on their income, property holdings, occupation, etc.	None
What is left is a group that meets constitutional muster.	None
It is a group right that must also belong to individuals, if the right is to have any meaning.	None
If one OBC candidate is denied special provisions that he should have received by law, it is not the groups responsibility to bring a claim.	None
He would be the one to do so.	None
He has a right of action to challenge the ruling that excluded him from the special provisions afforded to OBCs.	None
In this sense, he has an individual right.	None
Group and individual rights need not be mutually exclusive.	None
In this case, it is not one or the other but both that apply to the impugned legislation.	None
Whether the Creamy Layer exists outside India?	None
An interesting question arises does the concept of creamy layer exist outside India?	None
A 2003 study carried out in the United States suggests that it does.	None
The study by William Bowen, former president of Princeton University, found that when you look at students with the same Scholastic Aptitude Test (SAT) scores, certain groups have a better chance of being admitted to college.	None
The New Affirmative Action, by David Leonhardt, New York Times, 30 September 2007, p. 3.	None
All things being equal, ones chance of gaining admission is augmented by belonging to one of the preferred groups.	None
Individuals belonging to these groups are given preferential treatment over those who do not.	None
The study demonstrated that Black, Latino and NativeAmericans with the same SAT scores as White or Asian students had a 28 better chance than the White or Asian students at gaining admission those whose parents attended the college had a 20 advantage over those whose parents did not and the poor received no advantage whatsoever over the rich.	None
(See New York Times article, p. 3.)	None
The statistics indicate that the failure to exclude the creamy layer ultimately leads to a situation in which deserving students are excluded.	None
When we revert to the Indian scenario, as long as the Government gives handouts to certain groups, the creamy layer therein will lap them up.	None
A scheme in which the poor receive no advantage can be remedied by excluding the creamy layer.	None
Even the Mandal Commission, which was established in 1979 with a mandate to identify the socially and educationally backward, admitted that the creamy layer was robbing fellow OBCs of reservation.	None
In reference to Tamil Nadu, it said In actual operation, the benefits of reservation have gone primarily to the relatively more advanced castes amongst the notified backward classes.	None
(See P.37, 8.13 of the Report of the Backward Classes Commission, First Part, Vols. 12, 1980).	None
It also stated that it is no doubt true that the major benefits of reservation will be cornered by the more advanced sections.	None
but reasoned that this was acceptable because reform is presumably slow and should start with the more advanced of the backward.	None
(See Page 62, para 13.7 (recommendations)).	None
In N. M. Thomas Others case (supra), Krishna Iyer, J. in his concurring judgment in para 124 noted that the research conducted by the A.N. Sinha Institute of Social Studies, Patna, had revealed a dual society among harijans in which a tiny elite gobbles up the benefits.	None
Severing the Creamy Layer Technically speaking, I am severing the implied inclusion of the creamy layer.	None
It is severable for two reasons.	None
First, a nineJudge Bench in Sawhney I severed a similar provision wherein the creamy layer was not expressly included, upholding the rest of the O.M.s reservation scheme.	None
Second, because the Parliament must have known that Sawhney I had excluded the creamy layer, it seems likely that the Parliament also realized that this Court may do the same.	None
A cursory review of the Parliamentary Debates regarding Article 15(5) clearly reveals that the Parliament discussed the Sawhney I judgment in detail.	None
(See for example, comments made by Shri Mohan Singh, p.474 and Shri Devendra Prasad, pages 478479 on 21 December 2005).	None
Had the Parliament insisted on creamy layer inclusion, it could have said as much in the text of 15(5).	None
Instead, the Parliament left the text of 15(5) silent on the issue, delegating the issue of OBC identification to the executive in Section 2(g) of the Reservation Act.	None
The test for severability asks a subjective question had the Parliament known its provision would be struck would it still have passed the rest of the legislation?	None
(See R.M.D. Chamarbaugwalla Another v. Union of India Another, AIR 1957 SC 628 at page 637 at para 23).	None
It is never easy to say what the Parliament would have done had it known that part of its amendment would be severed.	None
Nevertheless, I find it hard to imagine that the Parliament would have said, if the creamy is excluded, the rest of the OBCs should be denied reservation in education.	None
It seems unlikely that it would have been an allornothing proposition for the Parliament, when the very goal of the impugned legislation of promoting OBC educational advancement does not depend on creamy layer inclusion.	None
For these reasons, I sever or exclude the implied inclusion of the creamy layer.	None
Identification of Creamy Layer Income as the criterion for creamy layer exclusion is insufficient and runs afoul of Sawhney I. (See page 724 at para 792).	None
Identification of the creamy layer has been and should be left to the Government, subject to judicial direction.	None
For a valid method of creamy layer exclusion, the Government may use its postSawhney I criteria as a template.	None
(See O.M. of 891993, para 2(c) Column 3, approved by this Court in Ashoka Kumar Thakur (supra), para 10).	None
This schedule is a comprehensive attempt to exclude the creamy layer in which income, Government posts, occupation and land holdings are taken into account.	None
The Office Memorandum is reproduced hereunder No	None
. 36012/22/93	None
Estt (SCT) Government of India Ministry of Personnel, Public Grievances Pension (Department of Personnel Training)	None
New Delhi, the 8th September, 1993 OFFICE MEMORANDUM Subject Reservation for Other Backward Classes in Civil Posts and Services under the Government of India  Regarding.	None
The undersigned is directed to refer to this Departments O.M. No.36012/31/90Estt(SCT) dated 13th	None
August, 1990 and 25th September, 1991 regarding reservation for Socially and Economically Backward Classes in Civil Posts and Services under the Government of India and to say that following the Supreme Court judgment in Indra Sawhney v. Union of India Others (Writ Petition (Civil) No.930 of 1990) the Government of India appointed an Expert Committee to recommend the criteria for exclusion of the socially advanced persons sections from the benefits of reservation for Other Backward Classes in civil posts and services under Government of India.	None
Consequent to the consideration of the Expert Committees recommendation this Departments Office Memorandum No.36012/31/90Estt.	None
(SCT), dated 13.8.1990 referred to in para (1) above is hereby modified to provide as follows (a) 27 (Twenty seven percent) of the vacancies in civil posts and services under the Government of India, to be filled through direct recruitment, shall be reserved for the Other Backward Classes.	None
Detailed instructions relating to the procedure to be followed for enforcing reservation will be issued separately.	None
Candidates belonging to OBCs recruited on the basis of merit in an open competition on the same standards prescribed for the general candidates shall not be adjusted against the reservation quota of 27.	None
(c) (i) The aforesaid reservation shall not apply to persons sections mentioned in column 3 of the Schedule to this Office Memorandum.	None
(ii) The rule of exclusion will not apply to persons working as artisans or engaged in hereditary occupations, callings.	None
A list of such occupations, callings will be issued separately by the Ministry of Welfare.	None
The OBCs for the purpose of the aforesaid reservation would comprise, in the first phase, the castes and communities which are common to both the lists in the report of the Mandal Commission and the State Governments Lists.	None
A list of such castes and communities is being issued separately by the Ministry of Welfare.	None
The aforesaid reservation shall take immediate effect.	None
However, this will not apply in vacancies where the recruitment process has already been initiated prior to the issue of this order.	None
Similar instructions in respect of public sector undertakings and financial institutions including public sector banks will be issued by the Department of Public Enterprises and by the Ministry of Finance respectively from the date of this Office Memorandum.	None

In sum, the schedule excludes the children of those who hold constitutional posts, e.g., the children of the President of India, Supreme Court Judges, Chairman and Members of UPSC and others are excluded.	None
Class 1 Officers children are not eligible for OBC perks either.	None
When both parents are ClassII	None
Officers, their children are excluded.	None
The same criteria that apply to ClassI and II officers apply to children of parents who work at high levels within the private sector.	None
Agricultural owners are excluded when their irrigated holdings are more than or equal to 85 of the statutory ceiling.	None
The O.M. further excludes persons having a gross annual income of Rs.2.5 lakh or more.	None
The Government raised the income limit from Rs.1 to Rs.2.5 lakh on 09.03.2004 vide O.M. 36033/3/2004.	None
The creamy layer schedule of the O.M. dated 8.9.93, in my opinion, is not comprehensive.	None
This should be revised periodically  preferably once in every 5 years, in order to ensure that creamy layer criteria take changing circumstances into account.	None
Apart from the people who have been excluded vide the office memo, I urge the Government to make it more comprehensive.	None
The Government should consider excluding the children of sitting and former Members of Parliament (MP) and Members of Legislative Assemblies (MLA) from special benefits.	None
If constitutional authorities have been excluded from benefits because of their status or resources, the same should apply to children of former and sitting MPs and MLAs.	None
I hope the judiciary will not have to involve itself in this matter.	None
Applying Article 21A to the Reservation Act On 18 December 2006, in the Rajya Sabha Debate on the Reservation Act, Member of Parliament and former Governor, Dr. P.C. Alexander summed up what would become one of Petitioners arguments.	None
Should Rs.17,000 crores be spent on implementing the Reservation Act for higher education when primary secondary schooling is in such bad shape?	None
Dr. Alexander stated Sir, this spending Rs.17,000 crores or whatever amount is needed for adding seats in the Engineering colleges, IIMs and IITs is reversing our priorities.	None
If you have the money for education, spend it on schools.	None
Spend it on the rural areas for primary schools spend it on the schools, which are poorly starved in the urban areas.	None
Instead of doing that, you spend it by adding to the numbers because you want to appease the socalled poorer sections in the higher castes.	None
So, we have taken care of you and you tell the backward classes we are taking care of all of you.	None
This is where we land ourselves in trouble.	None
We have cash resources.	None
They should be spent where priorities are fixed clearly in our eyes and we dont want to do that.	None
Spending on higher at the expense of lower education raises the specter of conflict with Article 21A.	None
By the 86th Amendment, Article 21A was inserted in our Constitution.	None
Article 21A reads as follows The State shall provide free and compulsory education to all children of the age of six to fourteen years in such manner as the State may, by law, determine.	None
Under Article 21A, it is a mandatory obligation of the State to provide free and compulsory education to all children aged six to fourteen.	None
In order to achieve this constitutional mandate, the State has to place much greater emphasis on allocating more funds for primary and secondary education.	None
There is no corresponding constitutional right to higher education.	None
The entire Nations progress virtually depends upon the proper and effective implementation of Article 21A. This Court in Unni Krishnan, J.P. Others v. State of Andhra Pradesh Others (1993) 1 SCC 645 para 166 held as under right to education is implicit in and flows from the right to life guaranteed by Article 21.	None
That the right to education has been treated as one of transcendental importance in the life of an individual and has been recognized not only in this country since thousands of years, but all over the world without education being provided to citizens of this country, the objectives set forth in the Preamble to the Constitution cannot be achieved.	None
The Constitution would fail.	None
This observation encouraged the Parliament to insert Article 21A into the Constitution.	None
In Unni Krishnan (supra), Justice Reddy observed that the quality of education in Government schools was extremely poor and that the schools were woefully inadequate to the needs of the children.	None
He noted that many countries spend 6 to 8 of Gross Domestic Product on education.	None
Our expenditure on education is just 4 of GDP.	None
Though an improvement over past performance, the overall education picture leaves much to be desired.	None
The bad news is really bad.	None
Even where we have seen improvement, there is still failure.	None
A survey by Pratham, an NGO, fleshes out the acute problems found in rural schools.	None
(See ASER 2007  Rural Annual Status of Education Report for 2007, published on January 16, 2008).	None
The survey covered 16,000 villages.	None
As Pratham indicates, there are an estimated 140 million children in the age group 6 to 14 years in primary schools.	None
Of these 30 million cannot read, 40 million can recognize a few alphabets, 40 million can read some words, and 30 million can read paragraphs.	None
Over 55 million of these children will not complete four years of school, eventually adding to the illiterate population of India.	None
The national literacy rate is 65. 63.	None
24 districts with more than 50,000 out of school children means we have failed 24 times over.	None
71 districts in which there are 60 students per teacher is just as bad, if not worse.	None
According to Pratham (and in line with the Ministry of HRDs sixmonth review), the number of out of school children has hovered around 7,50,000.	None
page 6.	None
Moreover, it goes without saying that children need proper facilities.	None
Today, just 59 of schools can boast of a useable toilet.	None
page 49.	None
The quality of education is equally troubling.	None
For standards I and II, only 78.3 of students surveyed could recognize letters and read words or more in their own language.	None
page 47.	None
In 2006, it was even worse  only 73.1 could do so.	None
It is disheartening to peruse the statistics for standards III to V, where only 66.4 could read Standard I text or more in their own language in 2007.	None
page 47.	None
As Pratham stated at page 7 What should be more worrying though, is the fact that in class 2, only 9 percent children can read the text appropriate to them, and 60 percent cannot even recognise numbers between 10 and 99.	None
In the third to fifth standards, 40 of students surveyed could not subtract.	None
The latest figures indicate that 58.3 children in the fifth standard read at the level appropriate for second Standard students.	None
page 32.	None
In both 2005 and 2007, only 74.1 of enrolled children were in attendance.	None
page 49.	None
The learned Solicitor General, Mr Vahanvati, submitted that the Government has now placed sufficient emphasis on primary education.	None
In 20012002, the Government launched Sarva Shiksha Abhiyan (SSA).	Arguments of Respondent
This national programmes goal is to universalize elementary education.	None
It supplements Governmental spending on education.	None
As the Solicitor General explained, it was founded on the idea that education for those between the ages of six to fourteen is a fundamental right.	None
In this way, SSA seeks to fulfill the Governments obligation under Article 21A to provide free and compulsory education to this age group.	None
Some of the SSAs accomplishments merit mention.	None
By March 2007, 2,03,577 toilets had been constructed or were under construction, covering 87 of the goal more than six crore free textbooks had been supplied  96 of the goal 1,93,220 new schools had been completed or were under construction, i.e., 80 of the desired mark.	None
The learned Solicitor General further provided that enrolment for all districts in 200405 for classes IV was 11,82,96,540.	None
In 200506, the number increased to 12,46,15,546.	None
A similar increase was seen in Classes VIVII VIII from 3,77,17,490 to 4,36,67,786.	None
The total number of teachers increased from 36,67,637 in 200304 to 46,90,176 in 200506.	None
It is the learned Solicitor Generals contention that SSA was responsible for many of the gains cited above.	None
This includes the improved statistics on the studentteacher ratio, out of school children and enrollment rate for girls.	None
While the Government is on the right track with regard to improving the infrastructure of our system, books and buildings only go so far.	None
They are necessary but not sufficient for achieving the ultimate goals of (1) keeping children in school, (2) ensuring that they learn how to think critically and (3) ensuring that they learn skills that will help them secure gainful employment.	None
The quality of education provided in the majority of primary schools is woeful.	None
That is why I find it necessary to review Government spending on education  especially at the primary secondary level.	None
Undoubtedly, the Government has allocated more funds of late for education, but we need to have far more allocation of funds and much greater emphasis on free and compulsory education.	None
Anything less would flout Article 21As mandate.	None
According to H.R.D. Annual Reports read with the Union of India Budget 200809, we spend roughly seven times as much on the individual college student than the individual primary or secondary student.	None

Government of India, Expenditure Budget Vol. 1, 20082009, p. 6, Total Expenditure of Ministries Departments (school education literacy and higher education have been added).	None
In a country where only 18 of those in the relevant age group make it to higher education, this is incredible.	None
See NSSO 19992000.	None
It is not suggested that higher education needs to be neglected or that higher education should not receive more funds, but there has to be much greater emphasis on the primary education.	None
Our priorities have to be changed.	None
Nothing is really more important than to ensure total compliance with Article 21A.	None
How can a sizeable portion of the population be precluded from realizing the benefits of development when almost everyone acknowledges that the children are our future?	None
Education for children up to the age of fourteen years should be free.	None
This has also been suggested in the recommendations of the Kothari Commission on Education in 1966.	None
Taking the countrys rampant poverty into account, free education up to the age 14 years is absolutely imperative.	None
There is no other way for the poor to climb their way out of this predicament.	None
Mr. P.P. Rao, learned Senior Advocate, rightly submitted that when you lack a school building, teachers, books and proper facilities, your schooling might be free but it is not an education in any proper sense.	None
Adequate number of schools must be established with proper infrastructure without further delay.	None
In order to achieve the constitutional goal of free and compulsory education, we have to appreciate the reality on the ground.	None
A sizeable section of the country is still so poor that many parents are compelled to send their children to work.	None
The State must carve out innovative policies to ensure that parents send their children to school.	None
The MidDay Meal Scheme will go a long way in achieving this goal.	None
But, apart from MidDay Meals, the Government should provide financial help to extremely poor parents.	None
In addition to free education and or other financial assistance, they should also be given books, uniforms and any other necessary benefits so that the object of Article 21A is achieved.	None
Time and again, this Court, in a number of judgments, has observed that the State cannot avoid its constitutional obligation on the ground of financial inabilities.	None
(See Hussainara Khatoon Others (III) v. Home Secretary, State of Bihar, Patna (1980) 1 SCC 98 , 107 at para 10).	None
In Vasanth Kumar (supra) at para 150, Justice Venkataramiah suggested that the State provide preferential treatment such as tuition, scholarships, free boarding and lodging, etc.	None
According to UNESCOs Education for All, Global Monitoring Report (2008) at page 115, at least fourteen countries have cashtransfer programmes that target poor households with schoolage children.	None
The largest programme is in Brazil, where 46 million people receive an education transfer of up to 44 USD monthly per household in extreme poverty with children below age 16.	None
According to the Report, the programme has reduced dropout rates by up to 75 among beneficiaries in its more recent stage.	None
Such a programme is not foreign to India.	None
According to UNICEF, the State of Gujarat put the idea of financial incentives for youth into action Figures indicate that the school enrolment drive of the state Government supported by incentives like Vidyalaxmi bond of Rs.1,000 given to each girl who completes primary education and 60 kg of wheat for tribal girls attending school, has met with significant success.	None
In addition to the various incentives by the Government, many a corporate houses and community have also come forward to motivate parents and children by donating school bags, uniforms, stationery, etc.	None
As a result, the dropout rate has come down from 35.31 in 19971998 to 3.24 in 20062007 in class 15.	None
In girls, this rate has dropped from 38.95 to 5.97 in the same time period.	None
In January 2008, Haryana Chief Minister Mr. Bhupinder Singh Hooda unfurled an incentive scheme for SC students in which students would receive a onetime payment in addition to a monthly stipend for attending school.	None
(See Incentives announced to curb dropout rate, The Tribune, 5 Jan. 2008).	None
The relevant portion is mentioned herein below Secretary, education, Rajan Gupta said a onetime allowance of Rs.740 to Rs.1,450 would be given to SC students from class I to XII.	None
Under the monthly incentive scheme, boys and girls studying in class I to V would be given Rs100 and Rs.150, respectively, per month and boys and girls of class VI to VIII Rs.150 and Rs.200.	None
Similarly, boys and girls of class IX to XII would be given Rs.200 and Rs.300, respectively, and boys and girls studying science subjects in class XI and XII Rs.300 and Rs.400, respectively.	None
This monthly incentive to the students would be deposited in their bank accounts to maintain transparency in the scheme, he added.	None
In the name of transparency, students attendance records could be made available to administrators and parents.	None
Students would be paid to attend school.	None
They would receive a sum for each day of school that they attended.	None
If you only attend 7 out of 10 school days, you would only receive 70 of the stipend.	None
Ultimately, this is the most important aspect of implementing Article 21A, incentives should be provided to parents so that they are persuaded to send their children to school.	None
More than punishment, creative incentive programmes will go a long way in the implementation of the fundamental right enshrined under Article 21A. Historical Perspective on Compulsory Education Almost two centuries ago, Clause 43 of The Charter Act of 1813 made education a State responsibility.	None
See Free and Compulsory Education Genesis and Execution of Constitutional Philosophy, Dr. P.L. Mehta and Rakhi Poonga, Deep and Deep Publications, New Delhi (1997).	None
pages 4247.	None
The Hunter Commission (188283) was the first to recommend universal education in India.	None
Thereafter, the Patel Bill, 1917 was the first compulsory education legislation.	None
It proposed to make education compulsory from ages 6 to 11.	None
The Government of India Act, 1935 provided that education should be made free and compulsory for both boys and girls.	None
Free and compulsory education got a further boost when the Zakir Hussain Commission recommended that the State should provide it.	None
The 1944 Sargent Report strongly recommended free and compulsory education for children aged six to fourteen.	None
By 1947, primary education had been made compulsory in 152 urban areas and 4995 rural areas.	None
The State has been making some endeavour to provide free and compulsory education since 1813 in one form or the other.	None
When the original Framers gathered at the Constituent Assembly, their desire to provide free and compulsory education was well established.	None
The real question in the Debate was whether the original Framers would make free and compulsory education justiciable or not.	None
They oscillated between the options, first placing it in the fundamental rights and later moving it to the directive principles of State policies under Article 45 of the Constitution.	None
Over 50 years later, the Parliament revisited the subject.	None
The Parliamentary debate on Article 21A offers a glimpse into the history of compulsory education in other countries.	None
The then Minister of Human Resource Development, Dr. M.M. Joshi, referred to the speech of Shri Gopal Krishna Gokhale on compulsory education.	None
While debating a bill in the imperial legislative council in 1911, Shri Gokhale said that in most countries elementary education is both compulsory and free, and in a few, though the principle of compulsion is not strictly enforced or has not been introduced it is either wholly or for the most part gratitutious, in India alone it is neither compulsory nor free.	None
Thus in Great Britain and Ireland, France, Germany, Switzerland, Austria, Hungary, Italy, Belguim, Norway, Sweden, the United States of America, Canada, Australia and Japan it is compulsory and free.	None
In Spain, Portugal, Greece, Bulgaria, Servia and Rumania, it is free, and in theory, compulsory, though compulsion is not strictly enforced.	None
Lok Sabha Debates, 28 November, 2001, Vol.20, page 476.	None
In 1948, the United Nations made its own pronouncement on compulsory education.	None
Article 26(1) of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights made free and compulsory education a lofty if not enforceable goal.	None
While many states consider it an authoritative interpretation of the United Nations Charter, the Declaration is not a treaty and is not intended to be legally binding.	None
Article 26(1) states Everyone has the right to education.	None
Education shall be free, at least in the elementary and fundamental stages.	None
Elementary education shall be compulsory.	None
Technical and professional education shall be made generally available and higher education shall be equally accessible to all on the basis of merit.	None
Our original Framers put a similar emphasis on the matter, placing free and compulsory education in the Directive Principles.	None
The unamended Article 45 provided that The State shall endeavour to provide, within a period of ten years from the commencement of this Constitution, for free and compulsory education for all children until they complete the age of fourteen years.	None
At this juncture, I deem it appropriate to refer to the Parliamentary Debate on the aspect of free and compulsory education.	None
In the Lok Sabha debate of 28 November 2001 at Vol. 20, Shri M.V.V.S. Murthi, at page 499, stated Unless the Government makes primary education compulsory, no village can develop.	None
If I say what they are doing in Andhra Pradesh, some Members may again cry foul.	None
In Andhra Pradesh, we are having Education Committees.	None
If there are any dropouts, the Committee will go to the village and find out the reason as to why they have dropped out.	None
It is very important.	None
The Report of the Kothari Commission, 19641966, headed by Prof. D. S. Kothari, provided important recommendations on compulsory education.	None
Nevertheless, the circumstances of the day compelled it to soften its suggestions.	None
The Nation was relatively poor and could not afford drastic increases in education spending.	None
Some excerpts of this report are reproduced as under 5.01.	None
But in any given society and at a given time, the decisions regarding the type, quantity and quality of educational facilities depend partly upon the resources available and partly upon the social and political philosophy of the people.	None
Poor and traditional societies are unable to develop even a programme of universal primary education.	None
But rich and industrialized societies provide universal secondary education and expanding and broadbased programmes of higher and adult education.	None
Feudal and aristocratic societies emphasize education for a few.	None
But democratic and socialistic societies emphasize mass education and equalization of educational opportunities.	None
The principal problem to be faced in the development of human resources, therefore, is precisely this How can available resources be best deployed to secure the most beneficial form of educational development?	None
How much education, of what type or level of quality, should society strive to provide and for whom?5.03 Increasing the Educational Level of Citizens.	None
In the next two decades the highest priority must be given to programmes aimed at raising the educational level of the average citizen.	None
Such programmes are essential on grounds of social justice, for making democracy viable and for improving the productivity of the average worker in agriculture and industry.	None
The most crucial of these programmes is to provide, as directed by Article 45 of the Constitution, free and compulsory education of good quality to all children up to the age of 14 years.	None
In view of the immense human and physical resources needed, however, the implementation of this programme will have to be phased over a period of time.	None
When Article 21A was introduced, some Members of Parliament argued that financially poor parents who fail to send their children to school should not be punished and that the word compulsion in this Article should be understood to apply exclusively to the State.	None
Let me examine this argument.	None
The 86th Amendment made three changes to the Constitution.	None
It added Articles 21A and 51A(k) and amended Article 45.	None
I turn my focus to Article 51A(k).	None
In addition to rejecting an amendment that would have neutered compulsory education, the Parliament made a positive gesture.	None
Though it never passed legislation seeking to implement compulsory education, it had not completely ignored the subject.	None
From Article 51A(k), it becomes clear that parents would be responsible for sending their children to school.	None
Article 51A read with 51A(k) is reproduced as under It shall be the duty of every citizen of India who is a parent or guardian to provide opportunities for education to his child or, as the case may be, ward between the age of six and fourteen years.	None
Just as Article 51A(a) does not penalize disrespect of the National Flag, Article 51A(k) does not penalize parents guardian for failing to send children to school.	None
There is, of course, legislation that gives teeth to Article 51A(a).	None
(See The Prevention of Insults to National Honour Act, 1971, Section 3A).	None
Article 51A(k) indicates that it is parents, not the State, who are responsible for making sure children wake up on time and reach school.	None
Thus, Article 21A read with Article 51A(k) distributes an obligation amongst the State and parents the State is concerned with free education, parents with compulsory.	None
Notwithstanding parental duty, the State also has a role to play in ensuring that compulsory education is feasible  a topic I will cover below.	None
The Central Government has made some effort to fulfill its obligation under Article 21A with regard to free education.	None
Sarva Shiksha Abhiyan is one such example.	None
When it comes to compulsory education, the Central Government has made no such effort.	None
The Parliament has not passed any legislation.	None
The executive has not issued any order.	None
What we have is a patchwork of different State and Union Territory laws.	None
These States UTs (and NCR) include Assam, Andhra Pradesh, Bihar, Chhatisgarh, Goa, Gujarat, Haryana, Himachal Pradesh, Jammu Kashmir, Karnataka, Kerala, Madhya Pradesh, Maharashtra, Orissa, Punjab, Rajasthan, Sikkim, Tamil Nadu, Uttar Pradesh, West Bengal, Delhi, Andaman Nicobar Islands.	None
The majority of the States and Union Territories levy very small fines on parents.	None
I note that these laws do not go into effect with one unexcused absence.	None
Notice is given to the parents, giving them time to remedy the problem.	None
Of course, enforcement is almost always a different story.	None
In contrast to the relatively light aforementioned sentences, the Compulsory Education Bill, 2006 introduced in the Rajya Sabha would provide six months imprisonment as a penalty for those who preclude children from going to school.	None
If this Bill becomes law, Section 7 would dictate the following If any person including parents of children prevents any boy or girl child from going to school or causes hindrance or obstruction in any way, he shall be punishable with imprisonment, which may extend to six months.	None
It seems that the Bill simultaneously targets employers and parents.	None
Employers would be punished when they hire a child to work too much or during school hours.	None
Similarly, parents would also be punished for allowing this to happen.	None
The Bill would also provide for scholarships, free hostel facilities and other incentives, whenever necessary and as may be prescribed.	None
In Bandhua Mukti Morcha v. Union of India Others, (1997) 10 SCC 549 at page 557 at para 11, the Court explained why education should be compulsory.	None
In essence, a citizen is only free when he can make a meaningful challenge to his fellow citizens or Governments attempt to curtail his natural freedom.	None
For this to happen, he needs a certain degree of education.	None
This is why Article 21A may be the most important fundamental right.	None
Without it, a citizen may never come to know of his other rights nor would he have the resources to adequately enforce them.	None
The relevant passage at para 11 reads as under A free educated citizen could meaningfully exercise his political rights, discharge social responsibilities satisfactorily and develop a spirit of tolerance and reform.	None
Therefore, education is compulsory.	None
Primary education to the children, in particular, to the child from poor, weaker sections, Dalits and Tribes and minorities is mandatory.	None
The basic education and employmentoriented vocational education should be imparted so as to empower the children within these segments of the society to retrieve them from poverty and, thus, develop basic abilities  to live a meaningful life  Compulsory education, therefore, to these children is one of the principal means and primary duty of the State for stability of the democracy, social integration and to eliminate social tensions.	None
In contrast to Article 51A(k), State and Union Territory laws and Parliamentary intent with regard to Article 21A, the Court in Mukti Morcha was inclined to suggest, not hold, that the State was exclusively responsible for compulsory education.	None
It went on to reaffirm M.C. Mehta v. State of Tamil Nadu Others (child labour matter) (1996) 6 SCC 756.	None
In that case, the Court took up the issue of child labour in hazardous fields when it learnt of an accident in a cracker factory in Sivakasi.	None
The said case at para 28 identified poverty as the root cause of child labour Of the aforesaid causes, it seems to us that  poverty is basic reason which compels parents of a child, despite their unwillingness, to get it employed.	None
The Survey Report of the Ministry of Labour (supra) had also stated so.	None
Otherwise, no parents, specially no mother, would like that a tenderaged child should toil in a factory in a difficult condition, instead of its enjoying its childhood at home under the paternal gaze.	None
In other words, parents send children to work because parents have no other choice.	None
Food comes first.	None
If the State does not provide extra income so as to remove the incentive to send children to work, it is wasting its time on mere gesture.	None
The Court in para 29 concluded that action must be taken It may be that child labour would be taken care of to some extent by insisting on compulsory education.	None
Indeed, Neera Burns thinks that if there is at all a blueprint for tackling the problem of child labour, it is education.	None
Even if it were to be so, the child of a poor parent would not receive education, if per force it has to earn to make the family meet both the ends.	None
Therefore, unless the family is assured of income aliunde, problem of child labour would hardly get solved and it is this vital question which has remained almost unattended.	None
We are, however, of the view that till an alternative income is assured to the family, the question of abolition of child labour would really remain willothewisp.	None
(emphasis added).	None
It is interesting to note that compulsory education has been introduced in one form or the other in various countries.	None
From the historical experience of these nations, we learn that the legislation pertaining to compulsory education has played an important role in improving educational outcomes.	None
Compulsory educations roots in the United States Compulsory education has had a long history outside of India.	None
In 1852, the State of Massachusetts enacted the first compulsory attendance law in the United States though compulsory education laws existed much earlier in many states, the first dating back to 1642 in Massachusetts.	None
Were Compulsory Attendance and Child Labor Laws Effective?	None
(See An analysis from 1915 to 1939.	None
(2001) at p. 2.	None
Prof. Adriana LlerasMuney of Princeton University.)	None
Reasons from abroad for implementing compulsory education Prof. LlerasMuney explains that those who advocated for compulsory education believed that universal education was necessary to promote democracy and guarantee a common American culture.	None
(Page 11).	None
Given the influx of immigrants, some of whom came from undemocratic countries, many supporters of legislation viewed compulsory education as an instrument for assimilation.	None
Other reasons cited by compulsory education proponents in the United States included the reduction of crime, racism and inequality.	None
Prof. Oreopoulos of the University of Toronto cites to sources that make it appear as though the reasons for adopting compulsory education in Canada mirrored those cited in the United States the emphasis was on good citizenship and economic development	None
Archibald Macallum, an Ontario teacher, summarized the latter argument vigorously in an 1875 report favouring the introduction of compulsory schooling in Canada Society has suffered so cruelly from ignorance, that its riddance is a matter of necessity, and by the universal diffusion of knowledge alone can ignorance and crime be banished from our midst in no other way can the best interests of society be conserved and improved than by this one remedy  the compulsory enforcement of this great boon  the right of every Canadian child to receive that education that will make him a good, loyal subject, prepared to serve his country in the various social functions which he may be called on to fill during his life and prepare him, through grace, for the life to come (Annual Report of the Ontario Teachers Association, 1875, as cited in Prentice and Houston 1975, 1756).	None
(See The Canadian Journal of Economics, Vol. 39, No.1, February (2006)	None
The compelling effects of compulsory schooling the evidence from Canada, Prof. Oreopoulos, at page 23).	None
Empirical data indicating that compulsory education has a positive effect Prof. Oreopoulos provides data that show the fruits of imposing education on citizens.	None
Crime may be lowered, health improved and civic activity increased.	None
Compulsory education may also lead to a substantial increase in income for individuals.	None
Moreover, compulsory education, if it does not cause, may at least contribute to an increase in bilingualism and employment and a reduction in poverty.	None
The relevant portion is reproduced hereunder (Page 24).	None
Other papers find evidence of social returns, but for nonpecuniary outcomes.	None
Lochner and Moretti (2002), for example, find that compulsory schooling lowers crime, while LlerasMuney (2002) finds a correlation with improved health.	None
In studies of the United States and United Kingdom, Dee (2003) and Milligan, Moretti, and Oreopoulos (2003) estimate that tighter restrictions on leaving school early correspond to increased levels of civic activity (like voting and discussing politics).	None
My analysis suggests that students compelled to complete an extra grade of school have historically experienced an average increase of 915 in annual income.	None
(Page 48).	None
I find that the introduction of tighter provincial restrictions on leaving school between 1920 and 1990 raised average grade attainment and incomes.	None
Students compelled to attend an extra year of school experienced an average increase in annual income of about 12.	None
I also find that compulsory schooling is associated with significant benefits in terms of other socioeconomic outcome measures ranging from bilingualism, employment, and poverty status.	None
These results hold up against many specifications checks and are entirely consistent with previous studies.	None
In addition to increased income, Prof. LlerasMuney found that legally requiring a child to attend school for one more year increased educational attainment by roughly five percentage points.	None
(Page 8).	None
Educational attainment refers to time spent in school.	None
Example of compulsory education statutes The causes of low enrolment, high dropout rates and frequent truancy in the U.S. and India differ, but the consequences thereof do not.	None
In either case, citizens who lack education are at an extreme disadvantage.	None
In India, poverty has been identified as the ultimate cause of lackluster enrolment and attendance rates.	None
Children are compelled to work.	None
In developed countries like the United States or Canada, children rarely fail to attend school because of economic constraints.	None
Instead, a number of different factors may contribute to truancy.	None
High school students may drop out because they detest school, lack motivation, or anticipate little reward from graduation.	None
(See The Canadian Journal of Economics, The compelling effects of compulsory schooling the evidence from Canada, Prof. Oreopoulos, p. 23, (quoting from Eckstein, Zvi, and Kenneth I. Wolpin (1999) Why youths drop out of high school the impact of preferences, opportunities, and abilities, Econometrica 67, 1295339).	None
As I detail below, students and parents in the United States often face the same fines when students fail to attend school.	None
Fines for students make more sense when low selfcontrol is the reason for which they fail to attend school.	None
At the same time, punishing Indian students who have no choice but to work would make no sense.	None
Such a punishment should not be borrowed from the United States.	None
In many jurisdictions in the United States, the attendance officer is responsible for enforcing compulsory attendance laws for his area or school.	None
Given the overwhelming problem of subpar enrolment and attendance in India, we doubt that one school official could sufficiently do the work of inspecting places of employment for children who have violated attendance laws.	None
Indeed, existing legislation in India already envisages the employment of attendance officers.	None
The Delhi Primary Education Act, 1960, Sec. 7.	None
