Relevant to the instant case, he explains that his amendment would allow the State to provide SC ST special treatment in regard to education.	None
In other words, Prof. Shah effectively wanted the equivalent to 15(4) and 15(5) but did not get it.	None
His amendment was negated.	None
(p. 664 of Constituent Assembly Debates, Vol. 7, 29 November, 1948).	None
Dr. Ambedkar disagreed with Prof. Shah on the limited ground that it would have given States the green light to segregate SC ST from general category students	None
The object which all of us have in mind is that the Scheduled Castes and Scheduled tribes should not be segregated from the general public.	None
For instance, none of us, I think, would like that a separate school should be established for the Scheduled Castes  If these words are added, it will probably give a handle for a State to say, Well, we are making special provision for the Scheduled Castes.	None
To my mind they can safely say so by taking shelter under the article if it is amended in the manner the Professor wants it.	None
page 661, CAD, Vol. 7, 29 November 1948.	None
Dr Ambedkar did not reject the Shah amendment because it would have allowed the States to implement affirmative action for SC ST in education.	None
He was concerned that special provisions would lead to negative discriminatory action in the guise of affirmative action.	None
Whether or not this would have happened is unclear, but his concern seems well placed.	None
A similar problem arises today, when the general category looks down upon or questions the qualifications of SC ST OBC professionals.	None
Though the individual may have earned admission on marks alone, others may presume that reservation was a factor.	None
Such a belief, regardless of veracity, cannot bode well for the career prospects of SC ST SEBCs.	None
Irrespective of the reason for which the Shah amendment was rejected, the original Framers contemplated special provisions for SC ST that would have included education.	None
At the end of the day, they decided that only women and children should benefit from discriminatory provisions.	None
Article 15(4) and the Shah amendment only differ in that Article 15(4) provides special provisions to SC ST and SEBC, while Shah only gave the same to SC ST.	None
Of course, if the original Framers rejected special provisions for SC ST, they would have done the same with respect to SEBC SC ST.	None
In sum, by limiting Article 15(3) to women and children and rejecting an amendment equivalent to Article 15(4), the original Framers intent was clear no special provisions for backward classes (SEBC SC ST) in education were to dilute Article 15(1)s prohibition against discrimination based on caste.	None
In the instant case, the Union of India argued that Article 15(4), the First Amendment to the Constitution, reflects the intent of the original Framers because it was passed by the same members that drafted the original Constitution.	None
In the Parliamentary debates in 1951, Prime Minister Nehru argued in favour amending the Constitution.	None
He and other Framers, as distinguished from the original Framers who had drafted the original Constitution, did not hide their disapproval of Champakam Dorairajan (supra).	None
Article 15(4) was to overturn that judgment.	None
To justify Article 15(4), which represented a dramatic departure from equality as envisaged in Articles 15(2), (3) and 29(2), Pandit Nehru said that Article 15(4) would give effect to what  was really intended or should be intended.	None
Yet, the original Framers, as explained above, had no intention of providing special provisions for SC ST in education (and a fortiori if not for them, nor for SEBC).	None
What should be intended is a far cry from what they specifically enacted and specifically rejected.	None
It follows that Article 15(4) deviated from the original Framers original intent.	None
Limitations on Reservation must be seen in the light of providing a casteless society Seeking to remove the blight created by caste, the original Framers were social reformers.	None
The social revolution meant to get (India) out of the medievalism based on birth, religion, custom, and community and reconstruct her social structure on modern foundations of law, individual merit, and secular education.	None
(See Granville Austin, Indian Constitution Cornerstone of a Nation at page 26, 1st Ed, 1972, Oxford University press (quoting from K. Santhanam (an Assembly member) in Magazine Section, The Hindustan Times New Delhi, 8 September 1946).	None
Indias first President Rajendra Prasad assured the Nation that the assembly and the Governments aim was to end poverty and squalor  to abolish distinction and exploitation and to ensure decent conditions of living.	None
Cornerstone at page 27, fn. 5 (quoting from Prasad in CAD V, I, 2).	None
The original Framers took steps to abolish castebased distinction.	None
For example, they outlawed untouchability in Article 17, promised all equal treatment before the law in Article 14, prohibited discrimination based on caste in 15(1) and 29(2) and selected joint over separate electorates.	None
The legislative reservations for SC ST were an exception to overarching goal of creating a casteless society that is why they were set to expire in 1960.	None
With respect to electorates, Granville Austin explains Desiring above all to promote national unity, members of the Constitutional Assembly rejected these devices by substituting direct elections for indirect in lower houses, by rejecting separate electorates in favour of joint electorates and by abolishing  except for Scheduled Castes and Tribes  reserved seats.	None
The Assembly believed, in Jennings words, that to recognize communal claims . .	None
.	Reasoning
is to strengthen communalism.	None
see Austin, p. 323 of Cornerstone.	None
(emphasis added)	None
The same can be said today.	None
Reservation based on caste strengthens communalism.	None
NonSEBCs naturally seek SEBC status so that they may capture SEBC benefits.	None
Upper castes, denied a seat, harbor ill will against lower castes who gain admission (whether it was by merit or not).	None
These feelings are the basis for discriminatory action.	None
On 16 September 2006, The Hindu reported While medical students at the All India Institute of Medical Sciences (AIIMS) have complained of caste discrimination, now doctors from the reserved category at the Guru Teg Bahadur Hospital (GTBH) too have written about biased attitude towards reserved category junior residents.	None
Discrimination is not the only problem exacerbated by reservation.	None
Given that reserved category students gain admission with lower marks, it also stands to reason that they would exhibit less confidence in their studies when pitted against the general category.	None
In her work on the unintended consequences of preferential treatment for minorities in college admissions in the United States, Marie Gryphon, a policy analyst for the Cato Institute (Washington, D.C.), writes recent research shows that affirmative action impedes academic achievement by undermining minority students confidence.	None
Preferences harm students selfimages, and this harm has practical costs in terms of grades and graduation rates.	None
Both studies build on earlier work by Stanford University sociologist Claude Steele, who coined the term stereotype threat to refer to the decline in performance suffered by members of groups who become afraid of confirming negative group stereotypes.	None
Steele tested his theory by giving standardized exams to groups of white and AfricanAmerican undergraduates at Stanford University.	None
Testers told some groups that the exam evaluated psychological factors related to testing, and that it was not a measure of ability.	None
They told other groups that the exam measured their intellectual abilities, and in some instances had them indicate their race on the exam.	None
The AfricanAmerican students who had been implicitly threatened with the stereotype of minority academic inferiority did markedly worse on the exam than black students in the other groups.	None
Even minority students who do not need preferences respond to an environment characterized by the relative academic weakness of minorities by worrying about confirming a negative stereotype.	None
Researchers also determined that vulnerability to Claude Steels stereotype threat is related to lower grades earned by minority students.	None
(See p. 910 (internal citations omitted), Executive Summary, No. 540, April 6, 2005, The Affirmative Action Myth.)	None
The point is that affirmative action produces consequences that may outweigh its supposed benefits.	None
To rid ourselves of reservation and its unintended consequences like casteism, we must focus our efforts on strengthening education at the primary and secondary level.	None
Only then will we achieve the casteless classless society the original Framers envisaged.	None
And only then will there be reason to scrap reservation altogether.	None
In his speeches to the Parliament regarding 15(4), Prime Minister Nehru could not have been clearer After all the whole purpose of the Constitution, as proclaimed in the Directive Principles is to move towards what I may say a casteless and classless society and in an attempt to achieve an egalitarian society, we want to put an end to all those infinite divisions that have arisen in our social life I am referring to the caste system and other religious divisions, call them by whatever name you like.	None
(emphasis added).	None
Parliamentary Debates on 13 June, 1951 and 29 May, 1951 respectively.	None
If reservation is allowed, then how can a casteless society still be realized?	None
This raises the issue of how beneficiaries of special provisions are to be classified.	None
As mentioned above, Mr. Salve and other learned counsel for petitioners pleaded that the Government cannot go forward with the Reservation Act when it has yet to identify its beneficiaries.	None
No one can say with certainty what percentage of the population is OBC, yet the Government is content with giving OBCs 27 of the seats in universities.	None
We do not know what proportion of the population is OBC because the census does not count OBCs.	None
It has been Central Government policy practically since Independence to avoid the question.	None
Eminent American Professor Mark Galanter writes that the absence of caste data was the deliberate policy of Sardar Patel, the Home Minister until 1950.	None
Mr. Patel rejected caste tabulation as a device to confirm the British theory that India was a casteridden country and as an expedient to meet the needs of administrative measures dependent on caste division (See Professor Marc Galanter, (1978)Who are the OBCs?	None
An Introduction to a Constitutional Puzzle.	None
13 Economic and Political Weekly 1812 at page 1824 at footnote 78 (quoting from Mr. Patels 1950 address to the census conference).	None
Taking an OBC census is horrifying because it encourages Government to enact policy on the basis of caste.	None
Doing so only furthers the castedivide, contrary to our constitutional aim.	None
This has been recognized since 1950.	None
If the Central Governments have consistently rejected an OBC census because it would promote casteism, how can this Central Government make reservation on the same ground?	None
It is one thing to ask a citizen his caste, it is even worse to grant or reject his college application on that ground.	None
The Government is between a rock and a hard place.	None
The only way out is to use exclusively economic criteria.	None
This would negate the need for a castebased census while ensuring that reservation go to the poor, the group for which the Reservation Act was purportedly passed.	None
The Parliament eventually settled on enabling States to provide provisions for socially and educationally backward classes.	None
Article 15(4).	None
This Court has interpreted backward classes to include caste as one of the criteria of classification under Article 16(4).	None
Sahwney I, para 859(3)(b).	None
In other words, caste falls under class according to Sawheny I, para 859(3)(a).	None
Economic criteria allows for reservation on grounds other than caste Despite the goal of a casteless society, the Parliament allowed for castebased reservation and, consequently, castebased discrimination.	None
Ultimately, they subjected Articles 29(2) and Article 15 to Article 15(4).	None
Dr. Ambedkar saw no choice but to discriminate based on caste, stating that if you make a reservation in favour of what are called backward classes which are nothing else but collection of certain castes, those who are excluded are persons who belong to certain castes.	None
Therefore, in the circumstances of this country, it is impossible to avoid reservation without excluding some people who have got a caste.	None
In draft article 10, Dr. Ambedkar tried to reconcile the view of those who were in favour of equality of opportunity with the demand of certain communities who remained neglected and who wanted to have a share in the administration.	None
In doing so, he was clear that the concept of equality, which is the very basis of democracy, should not be violated.	None
Part of his compromise meant that reservation had to remain reasonable.	None
Explaining his views on the matter, he said Supposing, for instance, we were to concede in full the demand of those communities who have not been so far employed in the public services to the fullest extent, what would really happen is, we shall be completely destroying the first proposition upon which we are all agreed, namely, that there shall be an equality of opportunity.	None
Let me give an illustration.	None
Supposing, for instance, reservations were made for a community or a collection of communities, the total of which came to something like 70 per cent of the total posts under the State and only 30 per cent are retained as the unreserved.	None
Could anybody say that the reservation of 30 per cent as open to general competition would be satisfactory from the point of view of giving effect to the first principle, namely, that there shall be equality of opportunity?	None
It cannot be in my judgment.	None
Therefore the seats to be reserved, if reservation is to be consistent with subclause (1) of Article 10, must be confined to a minority of seats.	None
(see CAD, Vol.7, 30th November, 1948 pp 70102).	None
On 17th November, 1949, the Constituent Assembly began the third reading of the Constitution Bill.	None
While replying to the debate, Dr. Ambedkar stated This anxiety is deepened by the realization of the fact that in addition to our old enemies in the form of castes and creeds we are going to have many political parties with diverse and opposing political creeds.	None
Will Indians place the country above their creed or will they place creed above country?	None
I do not know.	None
But this much is certain that if the parties place creed above country, our independence will be put in jeopardy a second time and probably be lost forever.	None
This eventuality we must all resolutely guard against.	None
We must be determined to defend our independence with the last drop of our blood.	None
(See CAD on 25th November, 1949 pp 977978) (emphasis supplied).	None
Exhibiting tunnel vision, our First Parliament failed to look beyond caste.	None
Another option was available, an option that adhered to the original Framers ideals.	None
Contrary to Dr Ambedkars view, it was possible to provide reservation to backward classes without discriminating based on caste.	None
Economic criteria target the poorest of the poor, irrespective of caste.	None
As noted, these criteria also simultaneously remove the creamy layer.	None
One of the other prominent advocates of reservation later realised that the policy did more harm than good.	None
Prime Minister Nehru wrote the following letter to the Chief Ministers on June 27th, 1961 I have referred above to efficiency and to our getting out of our traditional ruts.	None
This necessitates our getting out of the old habit of reservations and particular privileges being given to this caste or that group.	None
The recent meeting we held here, at which the chief ministers were present, to consider national integration, laid down that help should be given on economic considerations and not on caste.	None
It is true that we are tied up with certain rules and conventions about helping Scheduled Castes and Tribes.	None
They deserve help but, even so, I dislike any kind of reservation, more particularly in service.	None
I react strongly against anything which leads to inefficiency and secondrate standards.	None
I want my country to be a first class country in everything.	None
The moment we encourage the secondrate, we are lost.	None
The only real way to help a backward group is to give opportunities for good education.	None
This includes technical education, which is becoming more and more important.	None
Everything else is provision of some kind of crutches which do not add to the strength or health of the body.	None
We have made recently two decisions which are very important one is, universal free elementary education, that is the base and the second is scholarships on a very wide scale at every grade of education to bright boys and girls, and this applies not merely to literary education, but, much more so, to technical, scientific and medical training.	None
I lay stress on bright and able boys and girls.	None
I have no doubt that there is a vast reservoir of potential talent in this country if only we can give it opportunity.	None
But if we go in for reservations on communal and caste basis, we swamp the bright and able people and remain secondrate or thirdrate.	None
I am grieved to learn of how far this business of reservation has gone based on communal consideration.	None
It has amazed me to learn that even promotions are based sometimes on communal and caste considerations.	None
This way lies not only folly, but disaster.	None
Lets help the backward groups by all means, but never at the cost of efficiency.	None
How are we going to build our public sector or indeed any sector with secondrate people?	None
Upon expiry of the time limit, the criteria for identifying OBCs should only be economic in nature because our ultimate aim is to establish a casteless and classless society I am not the first to propose economic criteria as the exclusive means of identifying SEBCs.	None
In Vasanth Kumars case, counsel sought an opinion from the Court regarding reservations in employment and education for SC STs and OBCs.	None
The opinion would guide the Karnataka Government in implementing reservation.	None
para 1.	None
It serves our purposes to review their thorough analysis of the identification issue.	None
The Court in Vasanth Kumar observed as under 24.	None
No one is left in any doubt that the future Indian Society was to be casteless and classless.	None
Pandit Jawaharlal	None
Nehru the first Prime Minister of India said that Mahatma Gandhi has shaken the foundations of caste and the masses have been powerfully affected.	None
But an even greater power than Gandhi is at work, the conditions of modern life  and it seems at last this hoary and tenacious ralic of past times must die.	None
(Discovery of India by Pandit Nehru, Ch VI, p 234) Mahatma Gandhi, the Father of the Nation said, The caste system as we know is an anachronism.	None
It must go if both Hinduism and India are to live and grow from day to day.	None
In its onward march towards realising the constitutional goal, every attempt has to be made to destroy caste stratification.	None
Article 38(2) enjoins the State to strive to minimise the inequality in income and endeavour to eliminate inequalities in status, facilities and opportunities, not only amongst individuals but also amongst groups of people residing in different areas or engaged in different vocations.	None
Article 46 enjoins duty to promote with special care the educational and economic interests of the weaker sections of the people, and in particular, of the Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes, and shall protect them from social injustice and all forms of exploitation.	None
Continued retention of the division of the society into various castes simultaneously introduces inequality of status.	None
And this inequality in status is largely responsible for retaining inequality in facilities and opportunities, ultimately resulting in bringing into existence an economically depressed class far transcending caste structure and caste barrier.	None
The society therefore, was to be classless casteless society.	None
In order to set up such a society, steps have to be taken to weaken and progressively eliminate caste structure.	None
Unfortunately, the movement is in the reverse gear.	None
Caste stratification has become more rigid to some extent, and where concessions and preferred treatment schemes are introduced for economically disadvantaged classes, identifiable by caste label, the caste structure unfortunately received a fresh lease of life.	None
In fact there is a mad rush for being recognised as belonging to a caste which by its nomenclature would be included in the list of socially and educationally backward classes.	None
Rane Commission took note of the fact that there was an organised effort for being considered socially and educationally backward castes.	None
Rane Commission recalled the observations in Balaji case (1963) Supp (1)	None
SCR 439 that Social backwardness is on the ultimate analysis the result of poverty to a very large extent.	None
The Commission came to an irrefutable conclusion that amongst certain castes and communities or class of people, only lower income groups amongst them are socially and educationally backward.	None
In this judgment, this Court further observed that if State patronage for preferred treatment accepts caste as the only insignia for determining social and educational backwardness, the danger looms large that this approach alone would legitimize and perpetuate the caste system.	None
Castebased reservation does not go well with our secular character as enshrined in the Preamble to the Constitution.	None
That said, the majority in Sawhney I later sided with Justice Chinnappa Reddys view caste can be a factor in identifying SEBCs.	None
This view should not hold the day forever.	None
Eventually, the words of Justice Desai should be revived.	None
Justice Desai wanted to achieve two goals with one fell swoop of the pen.	None
Had his opinion prevailed (1) the creamy layer would have been removed ensuring that the truly deserving get the benefit and (2) the casteless society would have been furthered.	None
To these ends, he would have applied economic criteria to remove the creamy layer and simultaneously rid reservation of caste.	None
He explained that poverty is the bane of Indian society.	None
Given rampant poverty, it comes as no surprise that the bank balance, the property holding and the money power determine the social status of the individual and guarantee the opportunities to rise to the top echelon.	None
Vasanth Kumar at para 27.	None
As a result, the way wealth is acquired has lost significance.	None
And upper caste does not enjoy the status or respect any more even in rural areas what to speak of highly westernised urban society.	None
Finally, his Lordship recognized that creamy layer exclusion is inherently linked with identification based on economic criteria, i.e., occupation, income and land holdings If economic criterion for compensatory discrimination or affirmative action is accepted, it would strike at the root cause of social and educational backwardness, and simultaneously take a vital step in the direction of destruction of caste structure which in turn would advance the secular character of the Nation.	None
This approach seeks to translate into reality the twin constitutional goals one, to strike at the perpetuation of the caste stratification of the Indian Society so as to arrest progressive movement and to take a firm step towards establishing a casteless society and two, to progressively eliminate poverty by giving an opportunity to the disadvantaged sections of the society to raise their position and be part of the mainstream of life which means eradication of poverty.	None
Economic criteria must include occupation and land holdings because income alone is insufficient.	None
To decrease the likelihood that the undeserving evade identification, it is wise to employ more than one criterion.	None
In Vasanth Kumar, Justice Chinnappa Reddy departs from Justice Desais use of economic criteria as the sole means of identification.	None
Nevertheless, he recognizes that attainment of economic equality is the final and only solution to the besetting problems.	None
In Justice Chinnappa Reddys opinion, it is easier to classify based on caste than economic criteria 80 Class poverty, not individual poverty, is therefore the primary test.	None
Other ancillary tests are the way of life, the standard of living, the place in the social hierarchy, the habits and customs, etc. etc.	None
Despite individual exceptions, it may be possible and easy to identify socially backwardness with reference to caste, with reference to residence, with reference to occupation or some other dominant feature.	None
Notwithstanding our antipathy to caste and subregionalism, these are facts of life which cannot be wished away.	None
If they reflect poverty which is the primary source of social and educational backwardness, they must be recognised for what they are along with other less primary sources.	None
It all depends on how one defines class.	None
Once economic criteria remove the relatively wealthy families (from all castes and communities), a class will remain.	None
This class is known as the poor.	None
The class would share the same characteristic, irrespective of caste.	None
They would all lack money.	None
In a number of judgments, this Court has spelt out our constitutional philosophy regarding caste.	None
On numerous occasions, this Court has proclaimed that the cherished goal of the Nation is to realise a casteless society.	None
In Shri V. V. Giri v. Dippala Suri Dora Others (1960) 1	None
SCR 426 at 442, the Court observed as under The history of social reform for the last century and more has shown how difficult it is to break or even to relax the rigour of the inflexible and exclusive character of the caste system.	None
It is to be hoped that this position will change, and in course of time the cherished ideal of casteless society truly based on social equality will be attained under the powerful impact of the doctrine of social justice and equality proclaimed by the Constitution and sought to be implemented by the relevant statutes and as a result of the spread of secular education and the growth of a rational outlook and of proper sense of social values but at present it would be unrealistic and utopian to ignore the difficulties which a member of the depressed tribe or caste has to face in claiming a higher status amongst his coreligionists.	None
It is in the light of this background that the alternative plea of the appellant must be considered.	None
In N M. Thomas (supra), a seven Judge Bench observed as under This consummation is accomplished only when the utterly depressed groups can claim a fair share in public life and economic activity, including employment under the State, or when a classless and casteless society blossoms as a result of positive State action.	None
In his dissenting opinion, in Sawhney I Justice Kuldip Singh observed as under Secularism is the basic feature of the Indian Constitution.	None
It envisages a cohesive, unified and casteless society.	None
The prohibition on the ground of caste is total, the mandate is that never again in this country caste shall raise its head.	None
Even access to shops on the ground of caste is prohibited.	None
The progress of India has been from casteism and egalitarianism from feudalism to freedom.	None
The caste system which has been put in the grave by the framers of the Constitution is trying to raise its ugly head in various forms.	None
Caste poses a serious threat to the secularism and as a consequence to the integrity of the country.	None
Those who do not learn from the events of history are doomed to suffer again.	None
In Akhil Bhartiya Soshit Karamchari Sangh (Railway) (supra), it was observed as under These forces nurtured the roots of our constitutional values among which must be found the fighting faith in a casteless society, not by obliterating the label but by advancement of the backward.	None
Returning to Vasanth Kumar, one of Justice Reddys arguments deals with the level of effort required to identify the poor compared to the effort expended on identifying caste.	None
In the current context, a number of factors, including economic, are measured to determine SEBC status.	None
(See the National Commission of Backward Classes Guidelines for considerations of Requests for inclusion and complaints of underinclusion in the Central List of Other Backward Classes).	Arguments of Respondent
The National Commission for Backward Classes aside, I have set out to eventually install a system that only takes cognizance of economic criteria.	None
Using purely economic criteria would lighten the identification load, as ascertaining caste would no longer be required.	None
Respondents and others level a common criticism against the exclusive use of economic criteria.	None
Most of the country is poor.	None
Thus, too many people would be eligible for the benefit.	None
This is only a problem if you hand out reservations based on the groups proportion of the total population.	None
Such a reservation would be excessively unreasonable and would likely violate the Balaji cap of 50 see M.R. Balaji Ors.	None
v. State of Mysore (1963) Supp (	None
1) SCR 439.	None
If economic reservation were limited to a reasonable number, it could be upheld.	None
In addition to the problem of extending the benefit to too many, Reddy, J. cannot contemplate the idea of bestowing reservation on an economically poor Brahmin.	None
The idea that poor Brahmins may also be eligible for the benefits of Articles 15(4) and 16(4) is too grotesque even to be considered.	None
He says that they are not socially backward, thus they should not receive the benefit.	None
But can one call a Brahmin sweeper, poor by occupation, socially forward?	None
To do so would be a stretch.	None
The majority in Sawhney I reiterates Justice Chinnappa Reddys message in Vasanth Kumar.	None
They rejected the sole use of economic criteria to exclude the creamy layer, deeming it to be just one measure of advancement.	None
Justice Jeevan Reddy qualified that sentiment to an extent.	None
If income were extremely high, it could be the sole factor.	None
In such a case, income alone would ensure that one were socially forward.	None
Justice Jeevan Reddy was convinced that caste mattered more than money  especially in rural areas.	None
He makes his point by way of example at para 792	None
A member of backward class, say a member of carpenter caste, goes to Middle East and works there as a carpenter.	None
If you take his annual income in rupees, it would be fairly high from the Indian standard.	None
Is he to be excluded from the Backward Class?	None
Are his children in India to be deprived of the benefit of Article 16(4)?	None
Unless the carpenter became a factory owner, where his income would be a reflection of his status, Justice Reddy would answer his own question in the negative.	None
This is where we part ways.	None
Today, the NRI carpenters children will have likely attended the best schools, tuitions and coaching classes that money can buy.	None
These children do not need special provisions.	None
That is why I am removing the creamy layer, calling for a timelimit on castebased reservation and urging the Government to use exclusively economic criteria to identify OBCs who may avail of special provisions.	None
The United States Supreme Court has taken a similar position with regard to setting a timelimit on racebased affirmative action.	None
As mentioned above, Justice Sandra Day OConnor opined that there may be a timelimit to promoting diversity via preferential treatment for certain races We expect that 25 years from now, the use of racial preferences will no longer be necessary to further the interest approved today.	None
(See Grutter at 343).	None
In our context, one need not look past the Parliaments affinity with extending timelimits on reservation to see that only the judiciary can put a stop to castebased reservation.	None
Article 334 originally said that reservation for SC ST AngloIndians in the Lok Sabha and State Legislative Assemblies would expire on the Constitutions tenth birthday.	None
The Parliament later substituted ten for thirty years vide the 45th Amendment.	None
When that was to expire, the Parliament extended it for another ten years vide the 62nd Amendment.	None
When that was to expire, it extended it for another ten years vide the 79th Amendment.	None
History has shown that it is not politically feasible for the Parliament to say no to reservation  especially when caste is involved.	None
Nevertheless, I have noted that Sawhney I rejects purely economic criteria (occupation income property holdings or similar measures of economic power) with respect to classification under 16(4).	None
para 859, 4(a).	None
Sawhney Is nineJudge holding precludes us from striking the impugned legislation to the extent that it has not yet ruled out the use of castebased criteria for identifying SEBC status.	None
It also precludes us from forcing the Government to wean itself off castebased reservation by a certain date.	None
In order to achieve a casteless and classless society, after a lapse of ten years, special preference or reservation should be granted only on the basis of economic criteria as long as grave disparity and inequality persist.	None
Secularism is Part of the Basic Structure To be clear, there is no claim arising out of the goal to promote a casteless society.	None
No right of action exists.	None
The right of action is found in secularism.	None
Though not explicitly found in the unamended Constitution, the original Framers made it clear that India was to be a secular democracy.	None
Discrimination based on religion is prohibited by Articles 14, 15(1) and 15(2), 16(1) and 16(2), 29(2) and 325.	None
The original Framers went out of their way to ensure that minorities would be able to maintain their identity.	None
(See Articles 28, 29 and 30).	None
Article 27 precludes the state from adopting a state religion, whereas Article 25 grants citizens the right to profess, practice and propagate religion.	None
With rights come responsibilities.	None
One of them is found at Article 51A(3), which instructs citizens to promote harmony and spirit of brotherhood amongst all people  transcending religious  diversities.	None
Relying on these provisions, Bommai (1994) 3 SCC 1 at para 304 declared secularism a constitutional goal and a basic feature of the Constitution as affirmed in Kesavananda Bharati and Indira N. Gandhi v. Raj Narain.	None
Any step inconsistent with this constitutional policy is, in plain words, unconstitutional.	None
The Court reasoned that the original Framers adopted Articles 25, 26 and 27 so as to further secularism.	None
(See Bommai at para 28 (Ahmadi, J.)).	None
Secularism was very much embedded in their constitutional philosophy.	None
para 29.	None
During the Constituent Assembly Debates, Pandit Laxmikantha Mitra stated (as quoted at para 28 of Bommai)	None
By secular State, as I understand it, it is meant that the State is not going to make any discrimination whatsoever on the ground of religion or community against any person professing any particular form of religious faith  no citizen  will have any preferential treatment  simply on the ground that he professed a particular form of religion.	None
This is relevant today because quotas are statesponsored discrimination against those who are not deemed SEBCs  caste being a byproduct of religion.	None
Though affirmative action is allowed, there is a point at which it violates secularism.	None
Finally, I note that the 42nd Amendment, which formally inserted secularism into the Preamble, merely made what was already implicit explicit.	None
(See Bommai at para 29).	None
Conclusion on the Casteless Society In conclusion, the First Parliament, by enacting Article 15(5), deviated from the original Framers intent.	None
They passed an amendment that strengthens, rather than weakens casteism.	None
If castebased quotas in education are to stay, they should adhere to a basic tenet of secularism they should not take caste into account.	None
Instead, exclusively economic criteria should be used.	None
For a period of ten years, other factors such as income, occupation and property holdings etc. including caste, may be taken into consideration and thereafter only economic criteria should prevail.	None
Sawhney I has tied our hands.	None
I nevertheless believe that caste matters and will continue to matter as long as we divide society along castelines.	None
Castebased discrimination remains.	None
Violence between castes occurs.	None
Caste politics rages on.	None
Where casteism is present, the goal of achieving a casteless society must never be forgotten.	None
Any legislation to the contrary should be discarded.	None
Are Articles 15(4) and 15(5) mutually contradictory, such that 15(5) is unconstitutional?	None
While contradictory, I am able to read them harmoniously.	None
Learned senior counsel for petitioners, Mr. K.K. Venugopal, argued that Articles 15(5) and 15(4) are inconsistent to the extent that 15(5) exempts minority institutions from reservation and 15(4) incorporates aided minority institutions in the reservation scheme.	None
Because both provisions contain nonobstante clauses, they render each other void.	None
He further submitted that the Court is in the position of having to choose between them in regard to this inconsistency.	None
He provided three tests of statutory interpretation that give us guidance in resolving such a conflict.	None
First, if the Court cannot harmonize the two provisions, it must invalidate the one that completely destroys the others purpose.	None
Sarwan Singh Another v. Kasturi Lal (1977) 1 SCC 750 , pages 760761, at para 20).	None
In the instant case, one of the express purposes of 15(5) was to exempt minority institutions and thus avoid conflict with Article 30(1).	None
This is found in the text of Article 15(5) itself.	None
With nothing in the text of 15(4) to guide us, we turn to its Statement of Objects and Reasons The Act also amplifies Article 15(3) so as to ensure that any special provisions that the State may make for the educational, economic or social advancement of any backward class citizens may not be challenged on the ground of being discriminatory.	None
Thus, Article 15(4) was not passed with an express intention to include minority institutions nor did it arise out of a case in which minority institutions were a party.	None
Then again, it was open to the First Parliament to exclude minority institutions from the beginning.	None
Articles 15(4) and 15(5)s purposes do not necessarily conflict.	None
I find the first test inconclusive and thus turn to the other ones.	None
The second test asks which provision came into effect at a later date (i.e., was later in time?)?	None
That which is later shall prevail.	None
Here, 15(5) was enacted later in time.	None
In J.K. Cotton Spinning and Weaving Mills Co. Ltd. v. State of Uttar Pradesh Others AIR 1961 SC 1170 at page 1174, para 9, I find the third test it provides that the specific clause must trump the general.	None
Article 15(5) is specific in that it refers to special provisions that relate to admission in educational institutions, whereas 15(4) makes no such reference to the type of entity at which special provisions are to be enjoyed.	None
Because 15(5) is later in time and specific to the question presented, it must neutralize 15(4) in regard to reservation in education.	None
Mr K. Parasaran, learned senior counsel for the respondents, correctly pointed out that constitutional articles are to be read harmoniously, not in isolation.	None
(See T.M.A. Pai (supra) at page 582, para 148).	None
Our interpretation is harmonious because Article 15(4) still applies to other areas in which reservation may be passed.	None
Does Article 15(5)s exemption of minority institutions from the purview of reservation violate Article 14 of the Constitution?	None
Given the inherent tension between Articles 29(2) and 30(1), I find that the overriding constitutional goal of realizing a casteless classless society should serve as a tiebreaker.	None
We will take a step in the wrong direction if we subject minority institutions (even those that are aided) to reservation.	None
Minority aided institutions were subject to a limited form of reservation.	None
In order to preserve the minority character of the institution, reservation could only be imposed to a reasonable extent.	None
Minority aided institutions could select their own students, contingent upon admitting a reasonable number of nonminority students per the percentage provided by the State Government.	None
This conclusion was derived from two conflicting constitutional articles.	None
Of course, I am only concerned with minority aided institutions because I have already determined that the State shall not impose reservation on unaided institutions (minority or nonminority).	None
Article 30(1) provides that all minorities, whether based on religion or language, shall have the right to establish and administer educational institutions of their choice.	None
Article 29(2) states that no citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution maintained by the State or receiving aid out of State funds on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.	Arguments of Respondent
In other words, 30(1) by itself would allow minority aided institutions to reject all nonminority candidates, and 29(2) by itself would preclude the same as discrimination based solely on religion.	None
Yet neither provision exists by itself.	None
Rather than disturb the Constitution, this Court struck a compromise and diluted each provision in order to uphold both.	None
Reading Articles 30(1) and 29(2) harmoniously, Kerala Education Bill provided that once minority institutions receive aid, a sprinkling of outsiders must be admitted.	None
Sprinkling ensured that the minority character of the institution would not be lost.	None
In regard to the sprinkled seats, minority institutions cannot discriminate based on religion in violation of Article 29(2).	None
At the same time, if the State compelled aided minority institutions to take too many nonminority students, the institution would be minority in name only.	None
But what does too many mean?	None
Can sprinkling be quantified?	None
Clearing up the ambiguity, St. Stephens held that minority institutions must make 50 of their seats available to outsiders and that admission for the other 50 (its own community) must be done on merit.	None
Pai later rejected the rigidity attached to this fixed percentage.	None
Along these lines, Pai returned to a more flexible standard, one akin to sprinkling in Kerala Education Bill the moment a minority institution takes aid, it has to admit nonminority students to a reasonable extent, whereby the character of the institution was maintained and yet citizens Article 29(2) rights were not subverted.	None
(Also see Pai at para 149).	None
Thus, two admission pools were created for aided minority institutions minority and nonminority.	None
In the minority pool, merit was to be observed.	None
From the nonminority pool, reservations for the weaker sections may be made while the remaining seats, if any, would be distributed based on merit to nonminority students.	None
It would be open to the state authorities to insist on allocating a certain percentage of seats to those belonging to weaker sections of society, from amongst the nonminority seats.	None
Pai at para 152.	None
With regard to the percentage of reservation, the State Governments were to determine the percentage of nonminority seats according to the needs of that State.	None
As a compliment to reservation, aided minority institutions were also subject to regulation of administration and management.	None
Pai declared at para 72 as noted above that Once aid is granted to a private professional educational institution, the Government or the state agency, as a condition of the grant of aid, can put fetters on the freedom in the matter of administration and management of the institution.	None
The state, which gives aid to an educational institution, can impose such conditions as are necessary for the proper maintenance of the high standards of education as the financial burden is shared by the state.	None
In addition to the general power to impose conditions that seek to maintain high standards or excellence in education, the State could implement the same under a related but different rationale.	None
That is, said regulations could be upheld in the name of national interest.	None
Pai at para 107.	None
Yet the Government could not destroy the minority character of an institution.	None
para 107.	None
Nor could it obliterate the establishment or administration of a minority institution.	None
para 107.	None
A balance was to be struck between (a) maintaining academic quality and (b) preserving the minority right to establish administer educational institutions.	None
Regulations that embraced these two objectives were considered reasonable.	None
Pai at para 122.	None
A question of great import is whether Article 30 was designed to put minorities on equal or higher footing than nonminorities.	None
This question played out in detail in a debate between Khare, C.J. and Justice Sinha in Islamic Academy.	None
Writing for the majority, Chief Justice Khare takes issue with Pai.	None
The Chief Justice says that Pai has wrongly categorized minority rights as equal to those of the nonminority.	None
He has a point.	None
Minorities can establish and administer institutions for their communities per Article 30 nonminorities cannot.	None
His Lordship observed (para 9 page 723)	None
We do not read these paragraphs to mean that nonminority educational institutions would have the same rights as those conferred on minority educational institutions by Article 30 of the Constitution of India.	None
Nonminority educational institutions do not have the protection of Article 30.	None
Thus, in certain matters they cannot and do not stand on a similar footing as minority educational institutions.	None
Even though the principle behind Article 30 is to ensure that the minorities are protected and are given an equal treatment yet the special right given under Article 30 does give them certain advantages.	None
Relying on St. Xaviers case (1975) 1	None
SCR 173 , Pai concluded that the object of Article 30 was to ensure minorities of equal treatment and nothing more.	None
It was observed in St. Xaviers College case, at page 192, that the whole object of conferring the right on minorities under Article 30 is to ensure that there will be equality between the majority and the minority.	None
If the minorities do not have such special protection, they will be denied equality.	None
The minority institutions must be allowed to do what the nonminority institutions are permitted to do.	None
Pai at para 138.	None
In contrast to the majority in Islamic, Justice Sinha concludes that Article 30(1) raises minorities to an equal platform and no higher.	None
Relevant portion is reproduced hereinbelow	None
The statement of law contained in paras 138 and 139 is absolutely clear and unambiguous and no exception can be taken thereto.	None
The doubt, if any, that the minorities have a higher right in terms of Article 30(1) of the Constitution of India may be dispelled in clearest terms inasmuch as the right of the minorities and nonminorities is equal.	None
Only certain additional protection has been conferred under Article 30(1) of the Constitution of India to bring the minorities on the same platform as that of nonminorities as regards the right to establish and administer an educational institution for the purpose of imparting education to members of their own community whether based on religion or language.	None
see Islamic Academy at para 105.	None
Justice Sinha considers it constitutionally immoral to discriminate against nonminorities in the guise of protecting the constitutional rights of minorities.	None
See Islamic Academy at para 118.	None
Even in the face of Articles that provide preferential treatment to minority or weaker sections, e.g., 30(1), 15(4) and 16(4), the right to equality must mean something.	None
Justice Khare, as he then was, concludes that original Framers conferred Article 30(1) on minorities in order to instill in them a sense of confidence and security.	None
Pai at page 615 at para 229.	None
Their right to establish and administer educational institutions could not be usurped by mere legislation.	None
Khare, J. stated at para 229 p.615	None
Thus, while maintaining the rule of nondiscrimination envisaged by Article 29(2), the minorities should have also right to give preference to the students of their own community in the matter of admission in their own institution.	None
Otherwise, there would be no meaningful purpose of Article 30(1) in the Constitution.	None
True, the receipt of State aid makes it obligatory on the minority educational institution to keep the institution open to nonminority students without discrimination on the specified grounds.	None
But, to hold that the receipt of State aid completely disentitles the management of minority educational institutions from admitting students of their community to any extent will be to denude the essence of Article 30 of the Constitution.	None
It is, therefore, necessary that the minority be given preferential rights to admit students of their own community in their own institutions in a reasonable measure otherwise there would be no meaningful purpose of Article 30 in the Constitution.	None
Minorities possess one right or privilege that nonminorities do not establishing and administering institutions for their community.	None
The right to admit your own students in aided minority institutions was subject to admitting a reasonable number of outsiders.	None
In the instant case, aided minority institutions stand to benefit from the Reservation Act instead of having to admit a reasonable number of outsiders they would be exempted from reservation.	None
However, their nonminority counterparts would not.	None
Does this elevate their status?	None
While it does to a certain extent, however, we must also keep our constitutional goal and philosophy in mind.	None
Given the ultimate goal of furthering a classless casteless society, there is no need to go out on a limb and rewrite them into the Amendment.	None
Such a ruling would subject even more institutions to castebased reservation.	None
This would be a step back for the Nation, furthering the caste divide.	None
I refuse to go in that direction.	None
Are the standards of review laid down by the U.S. Supreme Court applicable to our review of affirmative action under Article 15(5) and similar provisions?	None
As noted above, U.S. law is, of course, not binding but does have great persuasive value.	None
This is because their problem of race is akin to our problem of caste.	None
Where others have reviewed similar issues in great detail, it behooves us to learn from their mistakes as well as accomplishments.	None
Mr. R. Venkataraman, former President of India in a foreword to a book of eminent constitutional expert Dr. L.M. Singhvi Democracy And Rule of Law Foundation And Frontiers, has aptly observed which reads as under Society progresses only by exchange of thoughts and ideas.	None
Imagine what a sorry state the world would have been in had not thoughts and ideas spread to all corners of the globe.	None
Throughout history, philosophers, reformers, thinkers, and scholars have recorded their thoughts, regardless of whether they were accepted or not in their times, and thus contributed towards progress of humankind.	None
India was the first to encapsulate this seminal global thought.	None
The Rig Veda says	None
Ano bhadrah Krtavo yantu	None
Viswatah Let noble thought come to us from every side.	None
With respect to OBC identification, was the Reservation Acts delegation of power to the Union Government excessive?	None
It is not an excessive delegation.	None
I agree with the Chief Justices reasoning at para 185 of his judgment.	None
Is the impugned legislation invalid as it fails to set a timelimit for castebased reservation?	None
It is not invalid because it fails to set a timelimit.	None
Given the Parliaments history of extending timelimits on other reservation schemes, there is much force to the argument that the Parliament will forever continue to extend reservations.	None
As noted above, it is consistent with our constitutional goal of achieving a classless casteless society that a timelimit be set.	None
But I am bound by Sawhney I and believe that only a larger bench could make such a ruling.	None
A larger bench could certainly hold that only economic criteria could be used to identify SEBCs and that it should be done by a certain date.	None
At what point is a student no longer Educationally Backward and thus no longer eligible for special provisions under 15(5)?	None
Once a candidate graduates from a university, he must be considered educationally forward.	None
Senior counsel for petitioners, Mr. P.P. Rao, contended that those who have completed Plus 2 should be considered educationally forward.	None
In other words, they would no longer be eligible for reservation in university or postgraduate studies.	None
There is some force in this argument where only 18 in the relevant agegroup have completed Plus 2.	None
From this vantage point, this means that they are educationally elite.	None
But the answer to most questions in law is not so simple.	None
The answer often depends on the circumstances surrounding the issue.	None
In the marketplace, a candidate who has completed higher secondary education cannot be considered forward.	None
The real value of the higher secondary degree is that it is a prerequisite for college admissions.	None
The general quality of education imparted upto Plus 2 is of extremely indifferent quality and apart from that, today some entrylevel Government positions only accept college graduates.	None
One is educationally backward until the candidate has graduated from a university.	None
Once he has, he shall no longer enjoy the benefits of reservation.	None
He is then deemed educationally forward.	None
For admission into Masters programmes, such as, Master of Engineering, Master of Laws, Master of Arts etc., none will be a fortiori eligible for special benefits for admission into post graduation or any further studies thereafter.	None
Would it be reasonable to balance OBC reservation with societal interests by instituting OBC cutoff marks that are slightly lower than that of the general category?	None
Balaji (supra) concluded that reservation must be reasonable.	None
The Oversight Committee has made a recommendation that will ensure the same.	None
At page 34 of Volume I of its Report, the Oversight Committee recommended that institutions of excellence set their own cut off marks such that quality is not completely compromised.	None
Cut offs or admission thresholds as suggested by the Oversight Committee are reproduced 4.4.2	None
The Committee recognizes that those institutions of higher learning which have established a global reputation (e.g. IITs, IIMs, IISc, AIIMS and other such exceptional quality institutions), can only maintain that if the highest quality in both faculty and students is ensured.	None
Therefore, the committee recommends that the threshold for admission should be determined by the respective institutions alone, as is done today, so that the level of its excellence is not compromised at all.	None
4.4.3	None
As regards cutoffs in institutions other than those mentioned in para 7, these may be placed somewhere midway between those for SC ST and the unreserved category, carefully, calibrated so that the principles of both equity and excellence can be maintained.	None
4.4.4 The Committee strongly feels that the students who currently tend to get excluded must be given every single opportunity to raise their own levels of attainment, so that they can reach their true potential.	None
The Government should invest heavily in creating powerful, well designed and executed remedial preparatory measures to achieve this objective fully.	None
Standards of excellence however should not be limited to the best aided institutions.	None
The Nation requires that its citizens have access to quality education.	None
Society as a whole stands to benefit from a rational reservation scheme.	None
Finding 68 reservation in educational institutions excessive, Balaji at pages 470471 (supra) admonished States that reservation must be reasonable and balanced against other societal interests.	None
States have to take reasonable and even generous steps to help the advancement of weaker elements the extent of the problem must be weighted, the requirements of the community at large must be borne in mind and a formula must be evolved which would strike a reasonable balance between the several relevant considerations.	None
To strike such a balance, Balaji slashed the impugned reservation from 68 to less than 50.	None
Balaji thus serves as an example in which this Court sought to ensure that reservation would remain reasonable.	None
We heed this example.	None
There should be no case in which the gap of cut off marks between OBC and general category students is too large.	None
To preclude such a situation, cut off marks for OBCs should be set no lower than 10 marks below the general category.	None
To this end, the Government shall set up a committee to look into the question of setting the OBC cut off at nor more than 10 marks below that of the general category.	None
Under such a scheme, whenever the noncreamy layer OBCs fail to fill the 27 reservation, the remaining seats would revert to general category students.	None
SUMMARY OF FINDINGS 1A. Whether the creamy layer be excluded from the 93rd Amendment (Reservation Act)?	None
Yes, it must.	None
The 93rd amendment would be ultra vires and invalid if the creamy layer is not excluded.	None
See paras 22, 25, 27, 30, 34, 35, 43, 44.	None
1B. What are the parameters for creamy layer exclusion?	None
For a valid method of creamy layer exclusion, the Government may use its postSawhney I criteria as a template.	None
(See Office Memorandum dated 891993, para 2(c) Column 3).	None
I urge the Government to periodically revise the O.M. so that changing circumstances can be taken into consideration while keeping our constitutional goal in view.	None
I further urge the Government to exclude the children of former and present Members of the Parliament and Members of Legislative Assemblies and the said O.M. be amended accordingly.	None
See paras 5557.	None
1C. Is creamy layer exclusion applicable to SC ST?	None
In Indra SawhneyI, creamy layer exclusion was only in regard to OBC.	None
Justice Reddy speaking for the majority at para 792 stated that this discussion is confined to Other Backward Classes only and has no relevance in the case of Scheduled Tribes and Scheduled Castes.	None
Similarly, in the instant case, the entire discussion was confined only to Other Backward Classes.	None
Therefore, I express no opinion with regard to the applicability of exclusion of creamy layer to the Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes.	None
See para 34.	None
Can the Fundamental Right under Article 21A be accomplished without great emphasis on primary education?	None
No, it cannot.	None
An inversion in priorities between higher and primary secondary education would make compliance with Article 21A extremely difficult.	None
It is not suggested that higher education needs no encouragement or that higher education should not receive more funds, but there has to be much greater emphasis on primary education.	None
Our priorities have to be changed.	None
Nothing is really more important than to ensure total compliance of Article 21A. Total compliance means good quality education is imparted and all children aged six to fourteen regularly attend schools.	None
I urge the Government to implement the following The current patchwork of laws on compulsory education is insufficient.	None
Monetary fines do not go far enough to ensure that Article 21A is implemented.	None
The Central Government should enact legislation that (a) provides lowincome parents guardians with financial incentives such that they may afford to send their children to schools (b) criminally penalizes those who receive financial incentives and despite such payment send their children to work (c) penalizes employers who preclude children from attending schools (d) the penalty should include imprisonment the aforementioned Bill would serve as an example.	None
The State is obligated under Article 21A to implement free and compulsory education in toto.	None
(e) until we have accomplished for children from six to fourteen years the object of free and compulsory education, the Government should continue to increase the education budget and make earnest efforts to ensure that children go to schools and receive quality education The Parliament should fix a deadline by which time free and compulsory education will have reached every child.	None
This must be done within six months, as the right to free and compulsory education is perhaps the most important of all the fundamental rights.	None
For without education, it becomes extremely difficult to exercise other fundamental rights.	None
See paras 126131.	None
Does the 93rd Amendment violate the Basic Structure of the Constitution by imposing reservation on unaided institutions?	None
Yes, it does.	None
Imposing reservation on unaided institutions violates the Basic Structure by stripping citizens of their fundamental right under Article 19(1)(g) to carry on an occupation.	None
T.M.A. Pai and Inamdar affirmed that the establishment and running of an educational institution falls under the right to an occupation.	None
The right to select students on the basis of merit is an essential feature of the right to establish and run an unaided institution.	None
Reservation is an unreasonable restriction that infringes this right by destroying the autonomy and essence of an unaided institution.	None
The effect of the 93rd Amendment is such that Article 19 is abrogated, leaving the Basic Structure altered.	None
To restore the Basic Structure, I sever the 93rd Amendments reference to unaided institutions.	None
See paras 132182.	None
Whether the use of caste to identify SEBCs runs afoul of the casteless classless society, in violation of Secularism.	None
Sawhney I compels me to conclude that use of caste is valid.	None
It is said that if reservation in education is to stay, it should adhere to a basic tenet of Secularism it should not take caste into account.	None
As long as caste is a criterion, we will never achieve a casteless society.	None
Exclusively economic criteria should be used.	None
I urge the Government that for a period of ten years caste and other factors such as occupation income property holdings or similar measures of economic power may be taken into consideration and thereafter only economic criteria should prevail otherwise we would not be able to achieve our constitutional goal of casteless and classless India.	None
See paras 194, 195, 231, 248, 251.	None
Are Articles 15(4) and 15(5) mutually contradictory, such that 15(5) is unconstitutional?	None
I am able to read them harmoniously.	None
See paras 252256.	None
Does Article 15(5)s exemption of minority institutions from the purview of reservation violate Article 14 of the Constitution?	None
Given the inherent tension between Articles 29(2) and 30(1), I find that the overriding constitutional goal of realizing a casteless classless society should serve as a tiebreaker.	None
We will take a step in the wrong direction if minority institutions (even those that are aided) are subject to reservation.	None
See paras 268269.	None
Are the standards of review laid down by the U.S. Supreme Court applicable to our review of affirmative action under Art 15(5) and similar provisions?	None
The principles enunciated by the American Supreme Court, such as, Suspect Legislation Narrow Tailoring Strict Scrutiny and Compelling State necessity are not strictly applicable for challenging the impugned legislation.	None
Cases decided by other countries are not binding but do have great persuasive value.	None
Let the path to our constitutional goals be enlightened by experience, learning, knowledge and wisdom from any quarter.	None
In the words of Rigveda, let noble thoughts come to us from every side.	None
See para 183.	None
With respect to OBC identification, was the Reservation Acts delegation of power to the Union Government excessive?	None
It is not an excessive delegation.	None
With respect to this issue, I agree with the reasoning of the Chief Justice in his judgment.	None
Is the impugned legislation invalid as it fails to set a timelimit for castebased reservation?	None
It is not invalid because it fails to set a timelimit.	None
See para 272.	None
At what point is a student no longer Educationally Backward and thus no longer eligible for special provisions under 15(5)?	None
Once a candidate graduates from a university, the said candidate is educationally forward and is ineligible for special benefits under Article 15(5) of the Constitution for post graduate and any further studies thereafter.	None
See para 273.	None
Would it be reasonable to balance OBC reservation with societal interests by instituting OBC cutoff marks that are slightly lower than that of the general category?	None
It is reasonable to balance reservation with other societal interests.	None
To maintain standards of excellence, cut off marks for OBCs should be set not more than 10 marks out of 100 below that of the general category.	None
See paras 274278.	None
These Writ Petitions and Contempt Petition are accordingly disposed of.	Decision
In the facts and circumstances, the parties are to bear their own costs.	Decision
